## Evelynn — 2026-04-22T06:23:40Z

**Bug #1 identified — CORS misconfig on dashboard service health cards.**

- `.env.local` points S2-S5 to Cloud Run URLs.
- Dashboard fetches `<svc>/health` client-side.
- S2-S5 respond `Access-Control-Allow-Origin: https://demo-studio-266692422014.europe-west1.run.app` (single hardcoded origin).
- Any other caller (127.0.0.1, any future demo-studio origin) gets blocked → DOWN badge.

Scope: all four services (S2/S3/S4/S5) have this — Jayce-3 CORS fix earlier only added the one prod origin.

Looking at `dashboard.html` before picking the fix approach.

   - **`tools/demo-studio-v3/tests/test_service_health_proxy.py`** (company-os, new file, 184 lines)
     - Created — 9 tests covering proxy contract
     - Fixture pattern:
       ```python
       @pytest.fixture
       def client(monkeypatch):
           monkeypatch.setenv("CONFIG_MGMT_URL", "https://fake-s2.example")
           monkeypatch.setenv("FACTORY_URL", "https://fake-s3.example")
           monkeypatch.setenv("VERIFICATION_URL", "https://fake-s4.example")
           monkeypatch.setenv("PREVIEW_URL", "https://fake-s5.example")
           import importlib
           import main
           importlib.reload(main)
           return TestClient(main.app)
       ```
     - Mock pattern using AsyncMock for httpx.AsyncClient:
       ```python
       mock_client = MagicMock()
       mock_client.__aenter__ = AsyncMock(return_value=mock_client)
       mock_client.__aexit__ = AsyncMock(return_value=False)
       mock_client.get = AsyncMock(return_value=mock_response)
       with patch("httpx.AsyncClient", return_value=mock_client):
           r = client.get(f"/api/service-health/{name}/health")
       ```
     - Committed first as xfail (`@pytest.mark.xfail(reason=_XFAIL_REASON, strict=True)`), then markers stripped via `sed -i '' 's/@pytest.mark.xfail(reason=_XFAIL_REASON, strict=True)//g'`

   - **`tools/demo-studio-v3/main.py`** (company-os, edited)
     - Added service health proxy route + edited `/dashboard` handler
     - New code inserted:
       ```python
       _SERVICE_HEALTH_ENV_MAP = {
           "s2": "CONFIG_MGMT_URL",
           "s3": "FACTORY_URL",
           "s4": "VERIFICATION_URL",
           "s5": "PREVIEW_URL",
       }

       @app.get("/api/service-health/{name}/health")
       async def service_health_proxy(name: str) -> JSONResponse:
           import httpx
           env_var = _SERVICE_HEALTH_ENV_MAP.get(name)
           if env_var is None:
               return JSONResponse({"detail": "unknown service"}, status_code=404)
           upstream_base = os.getenv(env_var, "").rstrip("/")
           if not upstream_base:
               return JSONResponse(
                   {"detail": f"upstream not configured ({env_var})"}, status_code=503
               )
           url = f"{upstream_base}/health"
           try:
               async with httpx.AsyncClient(timeout=5.0) as client:
                   resp = await client.get(url)
           except Exception as exc:
               return JSONResponse(
                   {"detail": f"upstream error: {type(exc).__name__}"},
                   status_code=502,
               )
           content_type = resp.headers.get("content-type", "")
           if content_type.startswith("application/json"):
               try:
                   body = resp.json()
               except Exception:
                   body = {"status": "error", "raw": resp.text}
           else:
               body = {"status": "ok" if resp.is_success else "error", "raw": resp.text}
           return JSONResponse(body, status_code=resp.status_code)
       ```
     - `/dashboard` service_urls dict changed from absolute Cloud Run URLs to relative proxy paths:
       ```python
       service_urls = {
           "s1Base": os.getenv("BASE_URL", ""),
           "configMgmt": "/api/service-health/s2",
           "factory": "/api/service-health/s3",
           "verification": "/api/service-health/s4",
           "preview": "/api/service-health/s5",
       }
       ```

## Duong — 2026-04-22T07:27:49Z

We want to seperate dashboard into another service, perhaps we could reuse this https://console.cloud.google.com/run/detail/europe-west1/demo-studio-mcp/observability/metrics?hl=de&project=mmpt-233505 and rename it? Is that possible?

## Evelynn — 2026-04-22T07:28:26Z

Short answer: **you can't rename a Cloud Run service** — service names are immutable once created. But there are a couple of clean paths to get what you want.

## Technical facts

- **Rename** — not supported. There is no `gcloud run services rename`. The name `demo-studio-mcp` is baked into the URL (`demo-studio-mcp-4nvufhmjiq-ew.a.run.app`) and its IAM resource ID.
- **Reuse the slot** — you can deploy a completely different container image to `demo-studio-mcp` and it'll serve dashboard traffic, but the URL stays misleading. Not recommended unless that URL is already wired into bookmarks/monitors you can't break.
- **Custom domain mappings** — if `demo-studio-mcp` has a custom domain (e.g. `dashboard.mmp.tech`), that mapping can be moved to a new service. The `*.run.app` URL cannot.

## Recommended path

1. **Create a fresh service: `demo-dashboard`** in `europe-west1 / mmpt-233505`. One `gcloud run deploy` call — trivial.
2. **Delete** `demo-studio-mcp` once the MCP retirement lands (per `plans/proposed/work/2026-04-21-demo-studio-mcp-retirement.md`). Or leave it stopped (min-instances=0) until retirement is confirmed.
3. **Reuse the observability setup** you linked (logs, metrics, alert policies) by pointing the same dashboards/alerts at the new service name.

## The harder question is the code split

Splitting the dashboard out of S1 (demo-studio-v3) isn't just a Cloud Run thing — it needs:

- **Code home** — new folder `tools/demo-dashboard/` in company-os, or its own repo
- **Shared concerns** — Firestore session reads, `/api/service-health/{name}` proxy (just landed in Loop 1), Firebase auth (Loop 2a server backbone) — duplicate vs factor into a shared lib
- **Routing** — separate `BASE_URL`, its own `deploy.sh`, its own `secrets-mapping.txt`
- **What moves** — `/dashboard` handler + `dashboard.html` + service-health proxy + `/api/test-results` + `/api/test-run-history` + `/api/managed-sessions` all migrate out of S1

This is plan-sized work — worth a quick ADR before execution. Want me to write one? The rough shape:

> Split `/dashboard` and its API surface out of `demo-studio-v3` into a new `demo-dashboard` Cloud Run service. Shared auth via the same Firebase cookie (once Loop 2b/2c land). S1 loses `/dashboard` + `/api/service-health/*` + `/api/test-*`.

Low confidence this should happen **before** Loop 2b (frontend sign-in) — because the dashboard benefits from Firebase auth too, and we'd rather do auth once. If you want to do it now, say the word and I'll draft the plan.

## Duong — 2026-04-22T07:29:58Z

Then let's create a new service for that, what's the differences between container, source and fucntion etc?

## Evelynn — 2026-04-22T07:30:26Z

Three deploy modes on Cloud Run, different trade-offs:

## 1. `--image` (container)
**You give Cloud Run a prebuilt OCI image.**
```bash
gcloud run deploy demo-dashboard \
  --image europe-west1-docker.pkg.dev/mmpt-233505/demo/demo-dashboard:v1 \
  --region europe-west1
```
- You own the Dockerfile + build pipeline.
- Fastest deploys once image is built; reproducible; can pin exact versions.
- Requires Artifact Registry (or Docker Hub) + a build step (Cloud Build, `docker buildx`, or CI).
- **This is what `demo-studio-v3` uses today** (`tools/demo-studio-v3/Dockerfile` + `deploy.sh` → Cloud Build).

## 2. `--source` (source-based)
**You point Cloud Run at a folder; it builds for you.**
```bash
gcloud run deploy demo-dashboard \
  --source ./tools/demo-dashboard \
  --region europe-west1
```
- Runs Cloud Build server-side. Detects Dockerfile → uses it; no Dockerfile → uses **Google Buildpacks** (auto-detects Python/Node/Go/etc.).
- One command, no Dockerfile needed for common stacks.
- Slower per deploy (rebuilds on Cloud Build each time), less reproducible if you rely on buildpack magic.
- Great for prototyping; can always migrate to `--image` later without changing the service.

## 3. Cloud Run Functions (née Cloud Functions 2nd gen)
**You give it a single function; Cloud Run wraps it.**
```bash
gcloud run deploy demo-dashboard-fn \
  --source . \
  --function main \
  --runtime python312 \
  --region europe-west1
```
- You write `def main(request): ...`; framework/server is auto-generated.
- For single-handler HTTP endpoints or event triggers (Pub/Sub, Cloud Storage).
- Wrong fit for a **multi-route FastAPI app** like the dashboard — you'd fight the abstraction.

## For `demo-dashboard` → use `--image` (container)

Reasoning:
- It's a multi-route FastAPI service, not a single function → Functions is wrong.
- Parity with `demo-studio-v3` and the four S2–S5 services keeps deploy/observability tooling uniform.
- `deploy.sh` pattern + `secrets-mapping.txt` + Cloud Build pipeline all copy-pasteable.
- Source deploy is fine for a one-off spike, but for something we'll iterate on, the Dockerfile + AR pipeline pays off fast.

Practical path:

1. Create `tools/demo-dashboard/` — copy Dockerfile + deploy.sh + requirements.txt skeleton from `demo-studio-v3`.
2. Move `/dashboard` handler + `dashboard.html` + `/api/service-health/*` + `/api/test-*` + `/api/managed-sessions` routes over. Keep Firestore session-read access (read-only is enough).
3. First deploy: `gcloud run deploy demo-dashboard --image … --region europe-west1 --allow-unauthenticated`.
4. Remove the migrated routes from `demo-studio-v3` in a follow-up commit.

Want me to write the split ADR now, or defer until after Loop 2b (so dashboard inherits Firebase auth from day one)? My recommendation is still: **defer past 2b, do the split when auth is ready** — otherwise you'll wire auth twice. But if you want a head start on the container scaffolding independent of auth, I can do that part first.

         "xfail: firebase_auth module not yet implemented. "

         return {
             "uid": uid, "email": email, "email_verified": email_verified,

   - **`tools/demo-studio-v3/firebase_auth.py`** (company-os, NEW file, impl)
     ```python
     class InvalidTokenError(Exception): ...
     class DomainNotAllowedError(Exception): ...
     
     @dataclass(frozen=True)
     class User:
         uid: str
         email: str
     
     def verify_firebase_token(id_token: str) -> User:
         if not id_token:
             raise InvalidTokenError("missing id_token")
         _init_firebase_admin()
         from firebase_admin import auth as fb_auth
         try:
             decoded = fb_auth.verify_id_token(id_token)
         except Exception as exc:
             raise InvalidTokenError(f"verify_id_token failed: {type(exc).__name__}") from exc
         if not decoded.get("email_verified", False):
             raise InvalidTokenError("email not verified")
         email = decoded.get("email", "").strip()
         allowed_domain = os.getenv("ALLOWED_EMAIL_DOMAIN", "").strip().lower()
         if not email.lower().endswith("@" + allowed_domain):
             raise DomainNotAllowedError(f"email domain not in allowlist: {email}")
         uid = decoded.get("uid") or decoded.get("sub") or ""
         return User(uid=uid, email=email)
     ```
     Lazy init handles ADC preference with FIREBASE_SERVICE_ACCOUNT_JSON fallback.

   - **`tools/demo-studio-v3/auth.py`** (company-os, additive edits)
     Added: USER_COOKIE_MAX_AGE = 7 * 86400, AUTH_LEGACY_COOKIE_ALLOWED = True
     ```python
     def encode_user_cookie(user: dict) -> str:
         uid = user.get("uid") or ""
         email = user.get("email") or ""
         if not uid or not email:
             raise ValueError("encode_user_cookie requires non-empty uid and email")
         payload = {"uid": uid, "email": email, "iat": int(time.time())}
         return _serializer.dumps(payload)
     
     def decode_user_cookie(cookie_value: str) -> Optional[dict]:
         if not cookie_value:
             return None
         try:
             data = _serializer.loads(cookie_value, max_age=USER_COOKIE_MAX_AGE)
         except Exception:
             return None
         if not isinstance(data, dict):
             return None
         if "uid" not in data or "email" not in data or "iat" not in data:
             return None
         return data
     ```

   - **`tools/demo-studio-v3/main.py`** (company-os, edits)
     - Added `from typing import Any, Optional`
     - Added to auth imports: USER_COOKIE_MAX_AGE, decode_user_cookie, encode_user_cookie
     - Added: `import firebase_auth as _firebase_auth_mod`
     - Inserted 4 routes before /auth/session/{sid}: /auth/config, /auth/login, /auth/logout, /auth/me
     ```python
     @app.post("/auth/login")
     async def auth_login(request: Request) -> Response:
         try:
             body = await request.json()
         except Exception:
             body = {}
         id_token = (body or {}).get("idToken", "")
         if not id_token:
             return JSONResponse({"detail": "missing idToken"}, status_code=400)
         try:
             user = _firebase_auth_mod.verify_firebase_token(id_token)
         except _firebase_auth_mod.DomainNotAllowedError as exc:
             return JSONResponse({"detail": f"domain not allowed: {exc}"}, status_code=403)
         except _firebase_auth_mod.InvalidTokenError as exc:
             return JSONResponse({"detail": f"invalid token: {exc}"}, status_code=401)
         cookie_value = encode_user_cookie({"uid": user.uid, "email": user.email})
         resp = Response(status_code=204)
         resp.set_cookie(key=COOKIE_NAME, value=cookie_value, httponly=True,
                         secure=_cookie_secure(), samesite="strict",
                         max_age=USER_COOKIE_MAX_AGE)
         return resp
     ```

## Evelynn — 2026-04-22T08:09:43Z

iTerm's fine — it's macOS file-descriptor exhaustion. Two unrelated things bit you:

**1. `ulimit` too low (256).** Every Claude Code session holds a bunch of FDs (MCP servers, IPC pipes, node watchers). 256 is macOS default and it's nowhere near enough once you've had a broken session leak FDs. Fix per the error:

```bash
ulimit -n 2147483646
claude
```

That raises it for the current shell. If it doesn't stick / you want it permanent:

```bash
sudo launchctl limit maxfiles 2147483646 2147483646
```

Then restart the terminal. Add `ulimit -n 65536` (or higher) to `~/.zshrc` so every new shell starts with enough headroom.

**2. The `source: operation not permitted` on `scripts/mac/aliases.sh`.** That's macOS quarantine / xattr on the file. Clear it:

```bash
xattr -d com.apple.quarantine ~/Documents/Personal/strawberry-agents/scripts/mac/aliases.sh
chmod +x ~/Documents/Personal/strawberry-agents/scripts/mac/aliases.sh
```

**Why now:** Probably the broken shell from earlier (the cwd-cache wedged session) didn't release FDs on exit. macOS keeps the count against your user until a reboot or until the parent processes fully die. `ulimit -n` bumps the ceiling so new `claude` can start even with the leak.

Once `claude` starts up again, the queue hasn't moved — dashboard-split promotion still needs the two suppressors + re-sign + re-promote, and Loop 2c plan needs a hook-compliant rewrite + clean commit.

## Duong — 2026-04-22T08:10:19Z

so what was the root cause and how can we mitigate this from the future?

## Evelynn — 2026-04-22T08:11:05Z

## Root cause

**Two distinct failures stacked:**

### 1. Claude Code harness wedged on cwd cache (primary)

When Ekko ran `scripts/plan-promote.sh`, the script `git mv`'d the plan file mid-execution. During that operation, the harness's cwd preflight check (which `stat`s the working dir before every Bash call) transiently failed — likely because the file-being-moved triggered a brief inode-level race on `/Users/duongntd99/Documents/Personal/strawberry-agents/`.

The harness **cached the failure for the entire session** and never re-validated. Every subsequent Bash call — mine, Yuumi's, Azir's, all three subagents — inherited the same broken parent state and died at preflight with "Working directory no longer exists" before a shell was ever spawned. Read tool kept working because it doesn't go through the cwd validator.

This is a Claude Code harness bug. The directory was fine the whole time.

### 2. macOS `ulimit -n 256` (secondary, revealed by trying to recover)

When you `/exit`'d and tried `claude` again, the broken session + its subagents + MCP servers had leaked FDs that macOS hadn't reclaimed yet. Default `ulimit -n 256` is far too low for Claude Code's baseline (MCP servers, node watchers, IPC pipes — easily 150+ FDs per session). Startup hit the ceiling and died.

### 3. Amplifier: concurrent coordinators (Evelynn + Sona) on same worktree

Evelynn was running in parallel during the same window. That caused the staging race that produced the mislabeled commit `252e024` (Azir staged Loop 2c, a concurrent Orianna-sign worker's `git add` displaced it, the wrong diff got committed under Azir's message). Not the root cause of the wedge but amplified the damage while it was happening.

---

## Mitigations (ranked by ROI)

| Fix | Effort | Impact |
|---|---|---|
| **Add `ulimit -n 65536` to `~/.zshrc`** | 30 sec | Prevents "can't even start claude" failure class entirely. Every future session inherits headroom. Highest ROI. |
| **Permanent `launchctl limit maxfiles`** | 1 min + reboot | Same thing, survives zsh-config drift. |
| **Document the "Bash-wedged → `/exit` immediately" pattern** | 2 min edit to `agents/evelynn/CLAUDE.md` + `agents/sona/CLAUDE.md` | When Bash preflight fails twice in a row with "cwd no longer exists," don't try to salvage — don't dispatch subagents (they'll all inherit + waste tokens producing elaborate failure reports, like today). Just `/exit` and reopen. |
| **Rule 3 enforcement: one coordinator per worktree** | Medium | Current rule says "use `git worktree` for branches," but we routinely run Evelynn and Sona in the same worktree for coordinator work. Either move one to a worktree, or add a "no concurrent index writes" protocol to both coordinator CLAUDE.mds (e.g. both coordinators touching `plans/` simultaneously is banned; one runs at a time). |
| **`plan-promote.sh` + `orianna-sign.sh`: hold an advisory lock** | Medium | Wrap the `git add` + `git commit` sequence in `flock` on a `.git/locks/strawberry-promote.lock`. Prevents concurrent-staging stomp like `252e024`. You already have `STAGED_SCOPE` for the related rename-aware problem (PR #20); an advisory lock is the lateral fix for concurrent workers of different scripts. |
| **File Claude Code issue for cwd-cache invalidation** | 10 min | Same shape as bug #29610 you already worked around. Won't fix it for us, but the engineering team should know. |

## Immediate action items

1. Persist `ulimit -n 65536` in your zshrc **now** so you don't get locked out next time.
2. Next coordinator session, before resuming the dashboard-split + Loop 2c work: I'll write up a `agents/evelynn/learnings/2026-04-22-bash-cwd-wedge-recovery.md` and a mirror in `agents/sona/learnings/` so the pattern is captured where both coordinators boot through it.
3. `flock`-wrapping the two scripts is a 30-minute Ekko task — queue it once we're unblocked on the plan promotions.

Want me to queue those as tasks now (blocked on the broken state clearing), or wait until you've re-run `claude`?

# /pre-compact-save — Pre-Compact Memory Consolidation

## When to use

- Before running `/compact` on an Evelynn or Sona coordinator session
- When the PreCompact hook blocks `/compact` and asks you to consolidate first
- When you want a mid-session snapshot without ending the session

## When NOT to use

- Subagent sessions (out of scope — Lissandra only handles coordinator sessions)
- Actual session end (use `/end-session` instead — it produces the full transcript archive)
- Immediately after a recent consolidation (redundant; worst case it produces a duplicate)

## Arguments

`` (optional): `evelynn` or `sona` to override auto-detection. Empty → auto-detect from session greeting.

## Protocol

1. **Preflight.**
   - Read the session jsonl path: `~/.claude/projects/<project-slug>/<session-id>.jsonl`. Derive `session_id` and `transcript_path` from the current environment.
   - If `` is non-empty, use it as the coordinator. Otherwise detect:
     - Scan the first 3 user messages for `Hey Sona` (case-insensitive) → coordinator = `sona`
     - Otherwise coordinator = `evelynn` (repo default per CLAUDE.md Caller Routing)
   - Cross-check `[concern: work]` vs `[concern: personal]` tags on subagent prompts. Contradiction → refuse with a diagnostic.

2. **Spawn Lissandra** via the Agent tool with `subagent_type: "Lissandra"`. Note: Lissandra updates `open-threads.md` and regenerates `INDEX.md` as part of the coordinator shard write, same as `/end-session` Step 6b. Prompt shape:

   ```
   [concern: <personal|work>]

   Consolidate this coordinator session before /compact. You are impersonating <coordinator>.

   - session_id: <uuid>
   - transcript_path: <absolute path to jsonl>
   - coordinator: <evelynn|sona>

   Run the full protocol in your agent definition (handoff shard, session shard, conditional learnings, journal entry, optional transcript excerpt, commit, sentinel). Write to `agents/<coordinator>/...` directories only. Use the coordinator's first-person voice.

   Report back with: artifact paths, commit SHA, push status, skipped steps (if any), warnings.
   ```

3. **On Lissandra return:**
   - Verify the sentinel file exists at `/tmp/claude-precompact-saved-<session_id>`. If not, report failure and exit — the PreCompact hook will still block on next `/compact`.
   - Verify the commit landed on main. `git log -1 --format='%H %s'` should show Lissandra's consolidation commit.
   - Report the artifact paths + commit SHA back to the coordinator.

4. **Done.** Coordinator can now safely run `/compact`; the PreCompact hook will see the sentinel and allow compaction.

## Failure modes

- **Coordinator detection contradiction** — refuse, surface the inconsistency. Duong resolves manually by supplying ``.
- **Lissandra commit rejected by pre-push hook** — Lissandra reports verbatim. Do not retry; let Duong diagnose.
- **No sentinel after Lissandra return** — indicates Lissandra's final step didn't fire. Report and exit without touching the sentinel ourselves (the sentinel is Lissandra's signature that she completed).

## What this skill does NOT do

- Does not run `/end-session`. That skill is `disable-model-invocation: true` for a reason.
- Does not compact. You still run `/compact` yourself after this skill succeeds.
- Does not archive the full session transcript. That is end-session's job.

# /check-inbox — read and archive pending inbox messages

Implements plans/in-progress/2026-04-20-strawberry-inbox-channel.md §3.4.

## Purpose

Scan `agents/<AGENT>/inbox/` for files with `status: pending`, display each
message, **archive** them to `agents/<AGENT>/inbox/archive/<YYYY-MM>/` with
`status: read` and a `read_at` timestamp. Enforces the pending-only invariant
of the main inbox directory.

After running, `agents/<AGENT>/inbox/` contains zero `status: pending` files.

## Step 0 — Identify the coordinator

Resolve agent name in this order:

1. `CLAUDE_AGENT_NAME` environment variable (set by `claude --agent <name>`)
2. `STRAWBERRY_AGENT` environment variable
3. `.claude/settings.json` `.agent` field (case-insensitive)

If none of the above resolves a name, refuse:

```
check-inbox: cannot identify agent — set CLAUDE_AGENT_NAME or STRAWBERRY_AGENT
```

## Step 1 — List pending messages

```bash
REPO_ROOT="$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel)"
ls "$REPO_ROOT/agents/<AGENT>/inbox/"*.md 2>/dev/null || echo "(no .md files)"
```

For each `.md` file found at the top level of `inbox/` (not in `archive/`
subdirectories), read its frontmatter and collect those with `status: pending`.

If none are pending, print:

```
No pending messages for <AGENT>.
```

...and stop (exit 0).

## Step 2 — Display each pending message

For each pending message file, print a formatted block:

```
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
From:      <from>
Priority:  <priority>
Timestamp: <timestamp>
File:      agents/<agent>/inbox/<filename>
──────────────────────────────────────────────────
<body text — everything after the closing --- frontmatter fence>
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
```

## Step 3 — Archive each message

For each pending message, perform the following steps **in order** (the
ordering is critical for watcher filter discipline — write `status: read`
before the `mv` so a concurrent watcher event sees the file already read):

### Step 3a — Rewrite frontmatter in place

Use the Edit tool:

- Change `status: pending` → `status: read`
- Add a new line `read_at: <ISO-8601 UTC timestamp>` directly after the
  `status: read` line.

Use `date -u +%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%SZ` via Bash for the timestamp.

Do not remove any other frontmatter fields. Do not alter the body text.

Example of updated frontmatter:

```yaml
---
from: sona
to: evelynn
priority: normal
timestamp: 2026-04-21T14:02:00Z
status: read
read_at: 2026-04-21T14:05:33Z
---
```

### Step 3b — Compute the archive path

- Derive `<YYYY-MM>` from the file's `timestamp:` frontmatter field.
  - Parse the first 7 characters (e.g. `2026-04` from `2026-04-21T14:02:00Z`).
  - Fallback: if `timestamp:` is absent, use the file's mtime:
    `date -r <file> +%Y-%m 2>/dev/null || date +%Y-%m`
- Archive path: `agents/<AGENT>/inbox/archive/<YYYY-MM>/<original-filename>`

### Step 3c — Move the file

```bash
mkdir -p "agents/<AGENT>/inbox/archive/<YYYY-MM>"
mv "agents/<AGENT>/inbox/<filename>" "agents/<AGENT>/inbox/archive/<YYYY-MM>/<filename>"
```

**Concurrency guard:** if the `mv` fails because the source file is already
gone (rare — would require two parallel `/check-inbox` runs on the same inbox),
skip and continue. Do not abort. This is idempotent by design.

## Step 4 — Summary

After processing all pending messages, print a one-line summary:

```
check-inbox: archived <N> message(s) for <AGENT>.
```

Post-condition: `agents/<AGENT>/inbox/` contains zero `status: pending` files.
The `archive/` subdirectory is the only remaining populated location.

## Refusal rules

- If the agent directory `agents/<AGENT>/` does not exist, refuse:
  `check-inbox: unknown agent <name>`
- If `agents/<AGENT>/inbox/` does not exist, print:
  `check-inbox: inbox directory not found for <AGENT> — no messages`
  and exit 0 (not an error; the inbox may never have been written to).
- Never write secrets into any message body.
- Never modify any field other than `status` and adding `read_at`.
- Never write to `archive/` from the `send` path — the `send` path in
  `/agent-ops` always writes to the flat `inbox/` directory only.

## Evelynn — 2026-04-22T10:05:32Z

No pending messages for sona.

# /check-inbox — read and archive pending inbox messages

Implements plans/in-progress/2026-04-20-strawberry-inbox-channel.md §3.4.

## Purpose

Scan `agents/<AGENT>/inbox/` for files with `status: pending`, display each
message, **archive** them to `agents/<AGENT>/inbox/archive/<YYYY-MM>/` with
`status: read` and a `read_at` timestamp. Enforces the pending-only invariant
of the main inbox directory.

After running, `agents/<AGENT>/inbox/` contains zero `status: pending` files.

## Step 0 — Identify the coordinator

Resolve agent name in this order:

1. `CLAUDE_AGENT_NAME` environment variable (set by `claude --agent <name>`)
2. `STRAWBERRY_AGENT` environment variable
3. `.claude/settings.json` `.agent` field (case-insensitive)

If none of the above resolves a name, refuse:

```
check-inbox: cannot identify agent — set CLAUDE_AGENT_NAME or STRAWBERRY_AGENT
```

## Step 1 — List pending messages

```bash

ls "$REPO_ROOT/agents/<AGENT>/inbox/"*.md 2>/dev/null || echo "(no .md files)"
```

For each `.md` file found at the top level of `inbox/` (not in `archive/`
subdirectories), read its frontmatter and collect those with `status: pending`.

If none are pending, print:

```
No pending messages for <AGENT>.
```

...and stop (exit 0).

## Step 2 — Display each pending message

For each pending message file, print a formatted block:

```
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

```

## Step 3 — Archive each message

For each pending message, perform the following steps **in order** (the
ordering is critical for watcher filter discipline — write `status: read`
before the `mv` so a concurrent watcher event sees the file already read):

### Step 3a — Rewrite frontmatter in place

Use the Edit tool:

- Change `status: pending` → `status: read`
- Add a new line `read_at: <ISO-8601 UTC timestamp>` directly after the
  `status: read` line.

Use `date -u +%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%SZ` via Bash for the timestamp.

Do not remove any other frontmatter fields. Do not alter the body text.

Example of updated frontmatter:

```yaml

to: evelynn
priority: normal

### Step 3b — Compute the archive path

  - Parse the first 7 characters (e.g. `2026-04` from `2026-04-21T14:02:00Z`).
  - Fallback: if `timestamp:` is absent, use the file's mtime:
    `date -r <file> +%Y-%m 2>/dev/null || date +%Y-%m`
- Archive path: `agents/<AGENT>/inbox/archive/<YYYY-MM>/<original-filename>`

### Step 3c — Move the file

```bash

```

**Concurrency guard:** if the `mv` fails because the source file is already
gone (rare — would require two parallel `/check-inbox` runs on the same inbox),
skip and continue. Do not abort. This is idempotent by design.

## Step 4 — Summary

After processing all pending messages, print a one-line summary:

```

```

Post-condition: `agents/<AGENT>/inbox/` contains zero `status: pending` files.
The `archive/` subdirectory is the only remaining populated location.

## Evelynn — 2026-04-22T10:09:31Z

**Preview iframe staleness — plan brief** (`c204d8f`, quick-lane, 4 tasks / 130min, target `feat/demo-studio-v3`):

**Problem:** `demo-preview` renders Allianz regardless of session brand. Fresh Aviva/Lemonade sessions still show Allianz chrome.

**Three hypotheses, none pre-decided:**
- **H1 — S2 seeding** — `demo-config-mgmt` seeds every session with Allianz default, never overwrites on brand change.
- **H2 — preview cache** — remote `demo-preview` service has a stale cache (module dict, warm container, or CDN) keyed wrong.
- **H3 — studio.js wiring** — iframe `src` never updates on brand change; `refreshPreview()` never fires or fires with bad URL.

**Tasks (strict order, Rule 12 xfail-first):**
1. **T1 (25min)** — Playwright xfail regression test: fresh session → commit Aviva brand → assert iframe shows Aviva, not Allianz. Lands before any fix.
2. **T2 (45min)** — Triage report with three probes: (a) hit S2 directly, (b) hit preview service bypassing studio.js with two session IDs, (c) Playwright-hook studio.js to see if/what `refreshPreview()` fires. Name dominant hypothesis with evidence.
3. **T3 (40min)** — Narrow fix on the dominant hypothesis branch only. ≤80 LOC, single-file where possible. No speculative fixes for the other two.
4. **T4 (20min)** — Flip xfail, run full live smoke (Aviva + Lemonade), save screenshot.

**Karma's prior (low-conf, must-disprove):** H3 dominates. Chat is brand-aware → S2 probably works (weakens H1). Per-container cache would vary per request → weakens H2. "iframe src never recomputes" is the canonical SPA preview failure mode.

**Three invariants the tests protect:**
- Inv-1: iframe contains brand-B chrome on brand-B session, no other brand chrome.
- Inv-2: brand change mid-session renders new brand within 10s.
- Inv-3: two concurrent different-brand sessions don't cross-contaminate (guards H2 regression class).

**Risks noted:** dominant-hypothesis misidentification (mitigation: revert T3 + re-triage if T4 red); demo-preview may be out-of-workspace deploy (escalate to Azir if so); iframe cross-origin flakiness (mitigation: assert on `src` URL + direct fetch, not iframe DOM).

## Duong — 2026-04-22T10:53:47Z

Base directory for this skill: /Users/duongntd99/Documents/Personal/strawberry-agents/.claude/skills/pre-compact-save

# /pre-compact-save — Pre-Compact Memory Consolidation

## When to use

- Before running `/compact` on an Evelynn or Sona coordinator session
- When the PreCompact hook blocks `/compact` and asks you to consolidate first
- When you want a mid-session snapshot without ending the session

## When NOT to use

- Subagent sessions (out of scope — Lissandra only handles coordinator sessions)
- Actual session end (use `/end-session` instead — it produces the full transcript archive)
- Immediately after a recent consolidation (redundant; worst case it produces a duplicate)

## Arguments

`` (optional): `evelynn` or `sona` to override auto-detection. Empty → auto-detect from session greeting.

## Protocol

1. **Preflight.**
   - Read the session jsonl path: `~/.claude/projects/<project-slug>/<session-id>.jsonl`. Derive `session_id` and `transcript_path` from the current environment.
   - If `` is non-empty, use it as the coordinator. Otherwise detect:
     - Scan the first 3 user messages for `Hey Sona` (case-insensitive) → coordinator = `sona`
     - Otherwise coordinator = `evelynn` (repo default per CLAUDE.md Caller Routing)
   - Cross-check `[concern: work]` vs `[concern: personal]` tags on subagent prompts. Contradiction → refuse with a diagnostic.

2. **Spawn Lissandra** via the Agent tool with `subagent_type: "Lissandra"`. Note: Lissandra updates `open-threads.md` and regenerates `INDEX.md` as part of the coordinator shard write, same as `/end-session` Step 6b. Prompt shape:

   ```
   [concern: <personal|work>]

   Consolidate this coordinator session before /compact. You are impersonating <coordinator>.

   - session_id: <uuid>
   - transcript_path: <absolute path to jsonl>
   - coordinator: <evelynn|sona>

   Run the full protocol in your agent definition (handoff shard, session shard, conditional learnings, journal entry, optional transcript excerpt, commit, sentinel). Write to `agents/<coordinator>/...` directories only. Use the coordinator's first-person voice.

   Report back with: artifact paths, commit SHA, push status, skipped steps (if any), warnings.
   ```

3. **On Lissandra return:**
   - Verify the sentinel file exists at `/tmp/claude-precompact-saved-<session_id>`. If not, report failure and exit — the PreCompact hook will still block on next `/compact`.
   - Verify the commit landed on main. `git log -1 --format='%H %s'` should show Lissandra's consolidation commit.
   - Report the artifact paths + commit SHA back to the coordinator.

4. **Done.** Coordinator can now safely run `/compact`; the PreCompact hook will see the sentinel and allow compaction.

## Failure modes

- **Coordinator detection contradiction** — refuse, surface the inconsistency. Duong resolves manually by supplying ``.
- **Lissandra commit rejected by pre-push hook** — Lissandra reports verbatim. Do not retry; let Duong diagnose.
- **No sentinel after Lissandra return** — indicates Lissandra's final step didn't fire. Report and exit without touching the sentinel ourselves (the sentinel is Lissandra's signature that she completed).

## What this skill does NOT do

- Does not run `/end-session`. That skill is `disable-model-invocation: true` for a reason.
- Does not compact. You still run `/compact` yourself after this skill succeeds.
- Does not archive the full session transcript. That is end-session's job.

## Duong — 2026-04-22T11:06:08Z

gcloud secrets add-iam-policy-binding DS_STUDIO_SESSION_SECRET \
  ▎   --member="serviceAccount:demo-dashboard-sa@mmpt-233505.iam.gserviceaccount.com" \
  ▎   --role=roles/secretmanager.secretAccessor --project=mmpt-233505
  ▎
  ▎ gcloud secrets add-iam-policy-binding DS_SHARED_INTERNAL_SECRET \
  ▎   --member="serviceAccount:demo-dashboard-sa@mmpt-233505.iam.gserviceaccount.com" \
  ▎   --role=roles/secretmanager.secretAccessor --project=mmpt-233505 why do we need this?

## Evelynn — 2026-04-22T11:06:21Z

Because `deploy.sh` uses `--set-secrets` to inject two env vars from Secret Manager at runtime:

```
--set-secrets="SESSION_SECRET=DS_STUDIO_SESSION_SECRET:latest,INTERNAL_SECRET=DS_SHARED_INTERNAL_SECRET:latest"
```

At container startup Cloud Run reads those secrets **as** the runtime SA (`demo-dashboard-sa`). Without `roles/secretmanager.secretAccessor` on each secret, the read 403s and the revision never becomes ready — the service fails to start at all.

What each secret is for:
- **`DS_STUDIO_SESSION_SECRET`** → `SESSION_SECRET` env var → signs/verifies the session cookie the dashboard sets on `/dashboard`.
- **`DS_SHARED_INTERNAL_SECRET`** → `INTERNAL_SECRET` env var → the `X-Internal-Secret` header gate on `/api/managed-sessions*` (the only non-public endpoints right now).

The legacy default compute SA already had these grants inherited from broad project roles — that's why demo-studio-v3 deploys "just worked." The scoped SA has zero inherited permissions by design (isolation: if S1 crashes/leaks, the dashboard SA can't touch anything else), so we have to grant each access explicitly.

If you'd rather not bother with Secret Manager for the internal gate, the alternative is to drop `--set-secrets` and set `INTERNAL_SECRET` as a plain `--set-env-vars` — but then the value sits in the Cloud Run revision config in plaintext, which is worse hygiene. Recommend keeping Secret Manager.

## Duong — 2026-04-22T11:07:28Z

it's fine if we use firebase auth for everything right? Then we wouldn't need to worry about these internal secret?

## Evelynn — 2026-04-22T11:07:42Z

Partly. It depends on **who calls those endpoints**.

- **If only the dashboard browser UI calls `/api/managed-sessions*`** (operator clicks "terminate" in the UI): yes — Firebase ID token on every request replaces `X-Internal-Secret` entirely. Drop the secret.

- **If another backend service calls it** (e.g. demo-studio-v3 hitting `/terminate` when a session expires): Firebase auth doesn't help — there's no user in that call path. But you still don't need a shared secret. The clean pattern is **Cloud Run IAM invoker**: mark `demo-dashboard` as requiring authenticated invocations, grant `roles/run.invoker` to the calling service's SA, and the caller attaches a Google-signed ID token automatically. Same isolation story, no secret to rotate.

Quick check worth doing: grep `demo-studio-v3` and the other services for any code that calls `/api/managed-sessions`. If none of them do (only the browser UI hits it), Firebase alone is sufficient and you can drop `DS_SHARED_INTERNAL_SECRET` + its grant entirely.

Want me to dispatch Ekko to grep the codebase and confirm the call graph before you commit to one or the other?

## Evelynn — 2026-04-22T13:12:15Z

Deployed to revision `demo-preview-00010-ff4`:

**What it is (PR #67 merged code):**
- Stdlib Python `ThreadingHTTPServer` (629 LOC) — ported from `origin/main`, replacing the FastAPI TODO-stub that hardcoded Allianz.
- Real Config-Mgmt integration: calls `CONFIG_MGMT_URL/config/{session_id}` if the env var is set. **Falls back to baked-in `configs/` dir if unset** — which is the concern I just sent Ekko to verify.
- Routes:
  - `GET /preview/{id}` — iframe-safe render (X-Frame-Options: ALLOWALL, CSP frame-ancestors *, Cache-Control: no-store)
  - `GET /preview/{id}/fullview` — standalone page, no X-Frame-Options
  - `GET /health` + `OPTIONS /health` — CORS headers
  - `GET /logs` — HMAC-gated in-memory ring buffer
  - `GET /static/*` — triple-guarded path traversal
- Session ID regex gate: `^[a-zA-Z0-9_-]{1,128}$` → 400 on invalid
- Jinja2 renders brand palette, market code, persona, template params from config

**What it is NOT:**
- Not FastAPI (main.py deleted)
- Not the Allianz-hardcoded stub
- Does not serve or touch any other service's code

**Commit range deployed:** `a20b361..ccd7a32` on `feat/demo-studio-v3` (includes the 4 PR #67 commits + QA-F1 test cleanup `c7db00c`).

## Evelynn — 2026-04-22T13:15:25Z

Answers your earlier "where does the config come from" question precisely:

**Session creation is empty — no brand.** `POST /session` just allocates an ID. Brand + palette + persona are written to `demo-config-mgmt` **later** by the managed agent during the Studio UI chat (when you say "I want Aviva" the agent writes the Aviva template into config-mgmt keyed by your session ID). `demo-preview` then reads that.

So the flow is:
```
You pick Aviva in Studio UI
  → managed agent writes Aviva config to demo-config-mgmt (session_id → palette/persona/market/etc)
    → preview iframe later reads demo-config-mgmt/config/{session_id}
      → renders Aviva
```

If config-mgmt has no doc for a session yet → returns Allianz default → preview shows Allianz. That's the "unknown session → Allianz" fallback we saw earlier.

**For your test** (Ekko's harness blocked the secret fetch — you need to run locally):

```bash
SECRET=$(gcloud secrets versions access latest --secret=DS_SHARED_INTERNAL_SECRET --project=mmpt-233505)

curl -s -X POST https://demo-studio-4nvufhmjiq-ew.a.run.app/session \
  -H "Content-Type: application/json" \
  -H "X-Internal-Secret: $SECRET" \
  -d '{"slackUserId":"duong-test","slackChannel":"test","slackThreadTs":"0.0"}' | tee /tmp/session-resp.json

SESSION_ID=$(jq -r .sessionId /tmp/session-resp.json)
echo "Studio:  https://demo-studio-4nvufhmjiq-ew.a.run.app$(jq -r .studioUrl /tmp/session-resp.json)"
echo "Preview: https://demo-preview-266692422014.europe-west1.run.app/preview/$SESSION_ID"
```

Then open Studio URL → chat with the agent → ask for Aviva. Once the agent writes the Aviva config, refresh the preview URL → you should see Aviva, not Allianz.

CONFIG_MGMT_TOKEN=dev-token \
  uvicorn main:app --host 127.0.0.1 --port 8002 --reload \
  --app-dir tools/demo-config-mgmt

```

`.env.local` needs: `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`, `FIRESTORE_PROJECT_ID=mmpt-233505`, `FIRESTORE_DATABASE=demo-studio-staging`, `SESSION_SECRET=dev-session-secret`, `INTERNAL_SECRET=dev-internal-secret`, **`COOKIE_SECURE=false`** (critical — cookie drops over plain HTTP otherwise), `CONFIG_MGMT_URL=http://localhost:8002`, `PREVIEW_URL=http://localhost:8090`, etc. Full list in the doc.

**Create session (no Slack/Firebase needed):**
```sh
curl -s -X POST http://localhost:8080/session \
  -H "Content-Type: application/json" \
  -H "X-Internal-Secret: dev-internal-secret" \
  -d '{"slackUserId":"local","slackChannel":"local","slackThreadTs":"0"}' | jq
```

## Evelynn — 2026-04-22T13:26:24Z

The server's using a different `INTERNAL_SECRET` than what you think. Two quick checks:

```sh
# In the terminal where S1 is running (or a fresh one after source):
echo "INTERNAL_SECRET=$INTERNAL_SECRET"
```

If it's empty or not `dev-internal-secret`, the source order is wrong — `.env` (with real prod-ish values from Secret Manager) is overriding `.env.local`.

**Fix:** source `.env.local` **after** `.env`, and make sure `.env.local` uses `export`:

```sh
cd tools/demo-studio-v3
# Make sure .env.local has: export INTERNAL_SECRET=dev-internal-secret
# not just: INTERNAL_SECRET=dev-internal-secret
set -a
source .env
source .env.local
set +a
uvicorn main:app --host 127.0.0.1 --port 8080 --reload
```

The `set -a` / `set +a` bracket auto-exports every var assigned in either file.

**Or simplest — inline override:**
```sh
INTERNAL_SECRET=dev-internal-secret curl -s -X POST http://localhost:8080/session \
  -H "Content-Type: application/json" \
  -H "X-Internal-Secret: dev-internal-secret" \
  -d '{"slackUserId":"local","slackChannel":"local","slackThreadTs":"0"}' | jq
```

Wait — that sets it on the client, not server. So the fix is: **restart uvicorn with the dev secret explicitly**:

```sh
cd tools/demo-studio-v3
INTERNAL_SECRET=dev-internal-secret SESSION_SECRET=dev-session-secret COOKIE_SECURE=false \
ANTHROPIC_API_KEY=$ANTHROPIC_API_KEY FIRESTORE_PROJECT_ID=mmpt-233505 \
FIRESTORE_DATABASE=demo-studio-staging CONFIG_MGMT_URL=http://localhost:8002 \
CONFIG_MGMT_TOKEN=dev-token PREVIEW_URL=http://localhost:8090 \
S5_BASE=http://localhost:8090 BASE_URL=http://localhost:8080 \
uvicorn main:app --host 127.0.0.1 --port 8080 --reload
```

Then your curl with `X-Internal-Secret: dev-internal-secret` will match.

## Duong — 2026-04-22T13:39:36Z

Base directory for this skill: /Users/duongntd99/Documents/Personal/strawberry-agents/.claude/skills/pre-compact-save

# /pre-compact-save — Pre-Compact Memory Consolidation

## When to use

- Before running `/compact` on an Evelynn or Sona coordinator session
- When the PreCompact hook blocks `/compact` and asks you to consolidate first
- When you want a mid-session snapshot without ending the session

## When NOT to use

- Subagent sessions (out of scope — Lissandra only handles coordinator sessions)
- Actual session end (use `/end-session` instead — it produces the full transcript archive)
- Immediately after a recent consolidation (redundant; worst case it produces a duplicate)

## Arguments

`` (optional): `evelynn` or `sona` to override auto-detection. Empty → auto-detect from session greeting.

## Protocol

1. **Preflight.**
   - Read the session jsonl path: `~/.claude/projects/<project-slug>/<session-id>.jsonl`. Derive `session_id` and `transcript_path` from the current environment.
   - If `` is non-empty, use it as the coordinator. Otherwise detect:
     - Scan the first 3 user messages for `Hey Sona` (case-insensitive) → coordinator = `sona`
     - Otherwise coordinator = `evelynn` (repo default per CLAUDE.md Caller Routing)
   - Cross-check `[concern: work]` vs `[concern: personal]` tags on subagent prompts. Contradiction → refuse with a diagnostic.

2. **Spawn Lissandra** via the Agent tool with `subagent_type: "Lissandra"`. Note: Lissandra updates `open-threads.md` and regenerates `INDEX.md` as part of the coordinator shard write, same as `/end-session` Step 6b. Prompt shape:

   ```
   [concern: <personal|work>]

   Consolidate this coordinator session before /compact. You are impersonating <coordinator>.

   - session_id: <uuid>
   - transcript_path: <absolute path to jsonl>
   - coordinator: <evelynn|sona>

   Run the full protocol in your agent definition (handoff shard, session shard, conditional learnings, journal entry, optional transcript excerpt, commit, sentinel). Write to `agents/<coordinator>/...` directories only. Use the coordinator's first-person voice.

   Report back with: artifact paths, commit SHA, push status, skipped steps (if any), warnings.
   ```

3. **On Lissandra return:**
   - Verify the sentinel file exists at `/tmp/claude-precompact-saved-<session_id>`. If not, report failure and exit — the PreCompact hook will still block on next `/compact`.
   - Verify the commit landed on main. `git log -1 --format='%H %s'` should show Lissandra's consolidation commit.
   - Report the artifact paths + commit SHA back to the coordinator.

4. **Done.** Coordinator can now safely run `/compact`; the PreCompact hook will see the sentinel and allow compaction.

## Failure modes

- **Coordinator detection contradiction** — refuse, surface the inconsistency. Duong resolves manually by supplying ``.
- **Lissandra commit rejected by pre-push hook** — Lissandra reports verbatim. Do not retry; let Duong diagnose.
- **No sentinel after Lissandra return** — indicates Lissandra's final step didn't fire. Report and exit without touching the sentinel ourselves (the sentinel is Lissandra's signature that she completed).

## What this skill does NOT do

- Does not run `/end-session`. That skill is `disable-model-invocation: true` for a reason.
- Does not compact. You still run `/compact` yourself after this skill succeeds.
- Does not archive the full session transcript. That is end-session's job.

## Duong — 2026-04-22T14:20:01Z

Please explain each in more simple and details

## Evelynn — 2026-04-22T14:20:40Z

Plain-English breakdown of each question:

---

**OQ-1 — How do we roll out the "real build" safely?**

The risk: the new real-build code could break and burn real Wallet Studio projects. We want to route only a small slice of users to the new version first, keep the old mock for the rest, then ramp up if it's stable.

Three ways to do the split:
- **(a) Revision traffic-split on the same service** — deploy new code as a new Cloud Run "revision," tell Cloud Run "send 10% of traffic to revision-new, 90% to revision-old." Flip to 100% when happy. One service, one URL, one log stream. This is the standard Cloud Run pattern.
- **(b) Spin up a whole second service** (`demo-factory-canary`) and put a load balancer in front. More moving parts, more config, same outcome.
- **(c) One service, one revision, but an env-flag** (`FACTORY_REAL_BUILD=true`) that toggles real vs mock at runtime. Atomic rollout — everyone flips at once.

Swain picked `a`. It's the cleanest and matches what ops already does.

---

**OQ-2 — When does the session know the build ID?**

When you click Build, S1 calls S3's `/build`. S3 returns a `buildId` and starts building in the background, streaming progress via SSE. The session doc in Firestore needs these IDs.

- **(a) Sync** — write `buildId` + `projectId` to the session doc immediately when S3's POST returns. One atomic write, no waiting.
- **(b) Async** — wait until the first SSE `build_started` event arrives, then write. Slightly safer if S3 crashes between "accepted" and "actually started."
- **(c) Both** — write sync, overwrite on async. Belt-and-braces.

Swain picked `a`. S3 already returns the IDs synchronously, no reason to wait.

---

**OQ-3 — How real is the integration test?** ⚠️ *matters for you*

We write a test that runs the full build pipeline end-to-end. Question is: does the test hit the **real** Wallet Studio staging API, or a **mock** that pretends to be WS?

- **(a) Real staging** — highest confidence. But every PR run talks to a real external service. Slow (minutes per run), flaky if WS has an outage, and costs real API calls.
- **(b) Full mock** — fast, hermetic, zero external dependencies. But if WS changes their API shape, we won't notice until prod.
- **(c) Hybrid** — PR runs use mock (fast CI), a nightly scheduled job runs the real version (catches WS drift within 24h).

Swain picked `c`. CI stays fast; drift gets caught daily. Your call if you'd rather pay the cost for real-every-PR or accept the mock-only risk.

---

**OQ-4 — What happens to half-built Wallet Studio projects?**

If a build fails halfway through (e.g., after `create_project` but before `publish`), we've created a WS project that nobody wants. Over time these accumulate.

- **(a) Ignore for now** — document the leakage, clean up later.
- **(b) Daily cleanup Cloud Run Job** — reads Firestore, finds abandoned projects, archives them.
- **(c) Archive on fail immediately** — the moment a build errors, delete the partial project.

Swain picked `a`. Ship the happy path first. Cleanup is a follow-up.

---

**OQ-5 — What if the progress stream breaks?** ⚠️ *matters for you*

S3 streams build progress to S1 over SSE. If the connection drops before the final `build_complete` event, S1 doesn't know if the build actually finished.

- **(a) Poll every 5s** — S1 hits `GET /build/{buildId}` in a loop until terminal. Robust but noisy.
- **(b) Rely on Firestore** — skip polling entirely, just read the latest state from Firestore. **Problem:** S3 doesn't currently write terminal state to Firestore, so picking this adds a new task.
- **(c) One-shot check on SSE close** — if the stream closes without a terminal event, hit `GET /build/{buildId}` exactly once to find out the final state.

Swain picked `c`. Minimal code, covers the realistic failure. If you'd rather go `(b)` — Firestore-first — we add a small S3 task to write terminal state to Firestore.

---

**OQ-6 — Where do the URL hostnames live?**

The iPad demo URL is `https://demo.missmp.tech/{shortcode}` and the project URL is `https://app.walletstudio.com/projects/{id}`. Those hostnames have to come from somewhere.

- **(a) Env vars** (`DEMO_BASE_URL`, `WS_APP_BASE_URL`) with prod defaults. Easy to override in stg.
- **(b) Hardcode** the prod hostnames in the Python file, refactor later.
- **(c) Fetch from a runtime config service** — overkill for two strings.

Swain picked `a`. Trivial to do, prevents a stg/prod parity bug where we accidentally link users to prod from staging.

---

**OQ-7 — Who designs the "Demo ready" panel?**

When the build finishes, the UI needs a new panel showing "Your demo is ready" with two buttons: iPad demo link + Wallet Studio project link. Design work needs a designer pass.

- **(a) Neeko full design** (wireframe + mockup + spec) → Seraphine implements. Complex-track, full ceremony.
- **(b) Lulu advises** in one shot ("here's the pattern, use the existing button styles") → Soraka implements. Normal-track, fast.
- **(c) Skip design** — Seraphine just writes it with existing CSS patterns.

Swain picked `b`. It's two lines of HTML with a primary button and a secondary link; Neeko-full is overkill.

---

**Bonus question — Can we run real-build at 100% in staging right away?**

Staging is a single-tenant sandbox — no real users, nothing to break. Swain recommends skipping the canary-split in staging and flipping real-build on at 100% from day one. Canary mechanics only kick in for prod.

---

If you're happy with all her picks, say "go with all defaults" and I'll promote + dispatch Aphelios. If you want to change any, just call out the numbers (e.g. "OQ-3 pick `a`, rest default").

## Duong — 2026-04-22T14:39:21Z

why does it take so long to promote the plan

## Evelynn — 2026-04-22T14:39:38Z

Bottleneck is **Orianna signing**, not the file move itself.

Orianna reads every load-bearing claim in the plan (paths, symbols, line numbers, shell commands, URL patterns) and grep-verifies each against the repo. For a 41KB structural ADR that's ~40+ claims to fact-check per run.

Common slowdowns:
1. **False positives need suppressor comments** — every path like `company-os/tools/demo-factory/main.py` or token like `httpx.AsyncClient` gets flagged unless annotated `<!-- orianna: ok — reason -->`. Each suppressor = 1 edit + 1 commit + 1 re-run.
2. **Two-repo drift** — Orianna runs against strawberry-agents and fact-checks paths in company-os (the *actual* workspace for the plan). Any unqualified path reads as "missing in this repo" and needs suppression. Swain pre-seeded 6 suppressors, but Ekko probably needs to add more.
3. **Body-hash invalidation** — if Ekko commits a suppressor during a sign run that's already in flight, the hash changes and Orianna rejects the sign attempt. Sequential only.
4. **Fact-check runs are ~30–60s each** — LLM call against the plan + repo grep batch.

Realistic budget for this plan: 3–6 sign iterations × ~60s + commit/push overhead = 5–10 min total. If Ekko gets stuck in a false-positive loop I'll step in.

Working on it in the background — will report when signed + promoted.

## Evelynn — 2026-04-22T14:41:35Z

Now I can see exactly what Ekko did wrong. The commit history on P1:

```

```

**What happened:**

1. Ekko signed at **21:30** (commit `2e18348`) — frontmatter got `orianna_signature_approved: sha256:898950...`. This step was fast.
2. Ekko then decided to **add two more "suppressor" comments** in the body (commit `8e14a83`) — polishing that wasn't needed.
3. Adding anything to the body changes the body-hash, which invalidates the signature. The script enforces this — so she **stripped `orianna_signature_approved` from the frontmatter** to go back to "proposed" state.
4. She then made a **second cosmetic body edit** (commit `46168f3`) reformatting my OQ decision block.
5. Two body edits later, she needed to re-sign from scratch — but instead of running `orianna-sign.sh` again, she **drifted onto a completely different plan** (staged-scope-guard-hook, which had its own stale signatures). She drove that plan through approved→in-progress→implemented with signatures + promotes, then wrote learnings, then ran out of budget / considered her work done.

**Root cause:** classic body-hash invalidation loop. She didn't need to touch the body after signing — the plan was already good. Two cosmetic edits cost her the signature, and her "fix everything that isn't signed" hygiene instinct pulled her onto the wrong plan.

I'll re-dispatch Ekko focused narrowly — sign only, no body edits, then promote.

## Evelynn — 2026-04-22T14:41:53Z

Re-dispatched with hard scope: sign, promote, push. No edits. Standing by.

## Duong — 2026-04-22T14:42:39Z

So this is Ekko not Orianna problem? How can we fix this to make sure he stays on track? Can you put this into feedback?

## Evelynn — 2026-04-22T14:42:51Z

Yes — Orianna did her job (fact-checked, signed, body-hash guard worked exactly as designed). This is an Ekko scope/discipline problem. Writing it up.

## Evelynn — 2026-04-22T14:43:48Z

Feedback committed: `feedback/2026-04-22-ekko-scope-drift-and-post-sign-body-edits.md` (commit `7571673`). Three proposed rules for the Ekko agent-def:

- **E1 — Signing is terminal for the phase.** No body edits after `orianna-sign.sh` succeeds. Re-sign required otherwise.
- **E2 — Scope lock.** One plan per dispatch. Noticed drift on other plans → report only, don't fix.
- **E3 — Sign → promote → push is atomic.** No interleaved work.

Also raised the open question of whether Ekko should even be the signer — or whether a `plan-signer` agent with no edit tools would structurally prevent this failure mode.

## Duong — 2026-04-22T14:46:02Z

## Evelynn — 2026-04-22T14:46:33Z

Here's the concrete shape I'd propose:

---

## plan-signer agent — scope sketch

### What it does (the only things)

1. Runs `bash scripts/orianna-sign.sh <plan-path> <phase>`.
2. Reads the script output.
3. If sign succeeds → runs `bash scripts/plan-promote.sh <plan-path> <phase>`.
4. If promote succeeds → runs `git push`.
5. Returns: final plan path, fact-check file path(s), sign commit SHA, promote commit SHA. That's the entire report.

### What it does NOT do

- **No body edits, ever.** Not even suppressor comments. Not even fixing typos it notices.
- **No fact-check interpretation.** If Orianna flags real issues that need plan body changes, the signer **stops and reports** — it does not decide what to fix.
- **No cross-plan work.** Exactly one plan per dispatch. If it notices another plan needs work, it reports and stops.
- **No learnings, no memory updates, no journal writes.** Coordinator handles those.
- **No PR creation, no deploy work, no secrets.** Out of scope by tooling.

### Tool allowlist (hard-narrowed)

- `Read` — to inspect the plan frontmatter before/after, and to read fact-check output files.
- `Bash` — gated to a script allowlist: only `scripts/orianna-sign.sh`, `scripts/plan-promote.sh`, `git status`, `git log`, `git push`, `git rev-parse`. No `git add`, no `git commit`, no `Edit`, no `Write`.
- **No** `Edit`, `Write`, `NotebookEdit`, or any MCP tool.

The `orianna-sign.sh` and `plan-promote.sh` scripts already do their own `git add` + `git commit` internally, so the signer doesn't need commit powers directly. This is the structural guarantee: **body edits are physically impossible** because the agent has no Edit/Write tool.

### The three failure branches

| What happens | What the signer does |
|---|---|
| Sign succeeds on first try → promote → push | Happy path. Report `iteration_count: 1`, paths, SHAs. |
| Orianna sign fails with suppressible false-positives (path tokens, URL tokens, etc. flagged as missing files) | **STOP and report**: here's the fact-check file, here are the claims flagged, coordinator decides whether to dispatch Syndra to add suppressors. Do NOT add them itself. |
| Orianna sign fails with real fact errors (wrong line number, nonexistent function, bad claim) | STOP and report: plan body is wrong, needs Swain/Karma to revise. Do NOT touch the body. |
| Sign succeeds but promote fails (hook rejects, pre-push blocks) | STOP and report the hook message verbatim. Do NOT try to work around it. |

### Model + cost

`sonnet` is overkill; the logic is script-invocation + if/else. Haiku is retired per rule 9. Use `sonnet` with a very tight prompt that emphasizes "your job is to run two scripts in order, report, and stop." Most invocations should be 5–10 tool calls max.

### What happens to Ekko

Ekko keeps DevOps execution: Cloud Run deploys, secret binding, `gcloud` work, learnings write-up, inbox-watch. Signing work moves off her plate entirely — which is the right fit anyway. Signing is a mechanical script invocation; Ekko's strength is judgment-heavy DevOps.

### Why this is structurally safer than "rules on Ekko"

Rules in a prompt are advisory — the agent can rationalize past them ("this small edit will help Orianna pass"). Removing the Edit/Write tools means the **failure mode is impossible to reach**, not just "forbidden". The agent physically cannot edit the plan body. That's the kind of constraint that actually holds.

### Chain placement

Coordinator → plan-signer (sign + promote + push). 

If sign fails with suppressor-needed claims → coordinator → Syndra (narrow tool scope, can edit agent-defs and plans within 1-2 lines) → coordinator → plan-signer (re-try).

If sign fails with real fact errors → coordinator → Swain/Karma (replan) → coordinator → plan-signer (re-try).

---

Want me to write the full `.claude/agents/plan-signer.md` agent-def and add a plan for rolling this out? It's a ~30-min plan to author the def + test it on the next signing dispatch.

## Duong — 2026-04-22T14:47:47Z

Ok then why not use Orianna herself?

## Evelynn — 2026-04-22T14:48:30Z

Good question — and the answer gets at a real architecture principle.

**Orianna already *is* the verifier, but she's deliberately not an Agent-callable entity.** Four reasons to keep her in that lane:

### 1. Separation of duties

The agent that **certifies** the plan ("these claims hold") should not also be the agent that **promotes** it ("move this forward"). That's the same anti-pattern as code review + merge by the same person. Today's split:

- **Orianna** signs: "I grep-verified every claim in this body, and I stamp the frontmatter with a hash."
- **Coordinator** (or an executor it dispatches) decides: "yes, promote it."
- **`plan-promote.sh`** enforces: "Orianna's signature must be valid before I'll move the file."

Collapsing Orianna into both roles removes the intermediate gate. The script becomes self-validating instead of externally-validated.

### 2. Orianna is script-only by design

She lives in `.claude/_script-only-agents/`, not `.claude/agents/`. She is **not callable via the Agent tool** — she's invoked as a subprocess by `orianna-sign.sh`. That's deliberate:

- Commits go under the `Orianna (agent) <orianna@agents.strawberry.local>` author identity.
- Her behavior is reproducible because the script wraps her invocation with the exact same prompt + context window every time.
- She can't drift off-task because she has no "session" — she's a pure function of (plan, phase) → (verdict, signature).

Making her Agent-dispatchable for workflow work would downgrade that boundary. Suddenly she has a conversation, can be interrupted, can be prompted into opportunistic work. That's how you get Ekko-shaped drift.

### 3. Her agent-def literally forbids it

From her description: *"Fails closed; **does not edit plans, only reports**."* She's designed as read-only at the plan level. The signature line is a very narrow exception — appended by the sign script wrapper, not by her own judgment. Giving her `git push` authority is scope creep past her stated contract.

### 4. Her prompt is tuned for paranoia, not workflow

She's optimized to be an adversarial grep-verifier: "find every claim and disprove it." That's the right headspace for verification. It's the wrong headspace for "run three scripts in order and report." Asking one agent to do both dilutes the verifier prompt and makes her less rigorous at her actual job.

---

### The cleaner mental model

```
  coordinator
      │
      ▼
  plan-signer ◄─── this is the new piece
      │
      │ invokes
      ▼
  orianna-sign.sh ──► spawns Orianna (script-only) ──► writes signature
      │
      ▼
  plan-promote.sh ──► checks Orianna's signature ──► moves file
      │
      ▼
  git push
```

Orianna is the **verification engine**. plan-signer is the **workflow driver**. The sign/promote scripts are the **protocol** connecting them. Three separate concerns, three separate actors — none of them can drift into the others' authority.

If we made Orianna the workflow driver, we'd collapse two layers and lose the auditing property that makes the gate trustworthy.

---

So: keep Orianna pure. Add plan-signer as a thin, tool-restricted executor. That's the shape.

Want me to write the plan-signer agent-def now?

## Duong — 2026-04-22T14:50:41Z

No, that makes thing too complicated. Orianna is the plan signer and she calls her tools to sign plan. That's it. It's just make sense. We don't need to create 2 person for a one person job. plan-signer is literally just bringing the plan to Orianna and bring her report back. Why not have Orianna do this herself? Why have the middle man

## Evelynn — 2026-04-22T14:51:28Z

You're right. I was over-engineering. Let me walk back my earlier argument honestly.

**My "separation of duties" point doesn't actually hold.** The signature itself IS the certification — the gate is in the script (`plan-promote.sh checks the signature`), not in the identity of who runs the script. Orianna running `plan-promote.sh` doesn't bypass anything, because the script verifies the signature the same way regardless of who invoked it. There's no second judgment being collapsed; there was only ever one judgment (the sign).

**The "script-only boundary" is a convention, not a physical law.** `.claude/_script-only-agents/` just means "not in the Agent-tool allowlist." Moving her out doesn't break anything load-bearing — the signing commit is still authored by `Orianna (agent) <orianna@agents.strawberry.local>` because that identity is configured in `orianna-sign.sh`, not derived from who dispatched her.

**"Read-only verifier" was me reading her agent-def too strictly.** The "does not edit plans" rule is about not silently modifying someone else's plan body during verification — not about never invoking scripts that mutate files. She already invokes Bash for grep and git operations during verification.

**The plan-signer was a middleman.** Its logic was: read path, call sign script, call promote script, call push, report. That's a pass-through with no judgment. Any discipline it had ("don't edit the body", "one plan per dispatch") is just prompt rules that can live on Orianna equally well.

---

### Concrete change for Orianna

Move her from `.claude/_script-only-agents/orianna.md` → `.claude/agents/orianna.md` and add to her description:

- She is now Agent-callable (and still script-callable, unchanged).
- Her job expands from "verify + sign" to "verify + sign + promote + push" — the full lifecycle transition.
- New discipline rules in her prompt:
  - **One plan per dispatch.** Never touch other plan files.
  - **Never edit the plan body** outside the signature line that `orianna-sign.sh` adds. If fact-check fails with suppressible false-positives, stop and report — don't fix.
  - **Sign → promote → push is atomic.** No interleaved work.
  - No learnings, journals, or memory updates — that's coordinator-side.
- Tool scope stays identical: Read, Glob, Grep, Bash. No Edit/Write — structurally prevents body drift, same as what I was proposing for plan-signer.

The `orianna-sign.sh` script still works unchanged; nothing about the verification pipeline breaks. The only difference is: when the coordinator wants a plan signed + promoted, it dispatches Orianna directly instead of Ekko.

Want me to draft the updated `orianna.md` and add it to the feedback doc as the recommended fix (replacing the plan-signer proposal)?

## Duong — 2026-04-22T17:08:38Z

Base directory for this skill: /Users/duongntd99/Documents/Personal/strawberry-agents/.claude/skills/end-session

# /end-session — top-level session close

You are closing a top-level Claude Code session. This skill wraps the full close-session protocol into a deterministic checklist. Follow every step in order. Do not skip steps. Do not reorder.

## Argument

`` is the agent name whose session is being closed. If empty, refuse immediately with `end-session: agent name required — pass the agent name as an argument (e.g. /end-session evelynn)` and exit. If `` is set to something other than a valid agent name (no matching `agents/<name>/` directory), refuse with `end-session: unknown agent <name>` and exit.

## Step 0 — Context probe

Run these Bash commands in a single call and keep the output in mind:

```
pwd
git status --short
git log -1 --oneline
date -u +%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%SZ
```

If the working tree has uncommitted changes unrelated to the session close (files outside `agents/<agent>/`, `scripts/`, `CLAUDE.md`, `.gitignore`), stop and report: `end-session: working tree dirty with unrelated files — commit or stash before closing`. Do not proceed.

## Step 1 — Discover source jsonl

Run the cleaner in dry-run mode (just discovery, no write) using the Bash tool:

```
python scripts/clean-jsonl.py --agent <agent> --session auto --out /tmp/end-session-probe.md
```

Note: for Phase 1, the cleaner does not have a separate dry-run flag. The `/tmp/` output path is a throwaway probe. After the probe, delete `/tmp/end-session-probe.md`.

Capture the stderr for any `CLEANER: chain ambiguous` warnings and relay them to the agent for confirmation before proceeding.

## Step 2 — Clean transcript

Run the cleaner for real:

```
python scripts/clean-jsonl.py --agent <agent> --session auto
```

The cleaner writes to the default path `agents/<agent>/transcripts/<YYYY-MM-DD>-<short-uuid>.md`.

- On exit code 0: record the output path from the cleaner's stdout.
- On exit code 1: report the error and stop. Do not proceed to any further step.
- On exit code 2: report the internal error and stop.
- On exit code 3: report the secret match verbatim, STOP IMMEDIATELY, do not stage any files, do not run the commit step. Escalate to Duong via the final report.

## Step 3 — Stage the transcript

```
git add agents/<agent>/transcripts/<YYYY-MM-DD>-<short-uuid>.md
```

Verify the file is staged with `git status --short`.

## Step 4 — (reserved for condenser, no-op in Phase 1)

Log `end-session: condenser step skipped — Phase 2 will wire Syndra's component A here` and continue.

## Step 5 — Journal append

Prompt the invoking agent (you, running this skill) to append their first-person reflection for this session to `agents/<agent>/journal/cli-<YYYY-MM-DD>.md`. Rules:

- Append only. Do NOT overwrite existing content.
- First-person voice. Not a transcript copy.
- 10–30 lines typical. No hard cap.

Use the Write tool if the file does not exist, Edit (append) if it does. After writing, stage the file:

```
git add agents/<agent>/journal/cli-<YYYY-MM-DD>.md
```

## Step 6 — Remember handoff

**If agent == evelynn:** Skip the `remember:remember` plugin entirely (it has a single-file race surface unsafe under concurrent close — see D6 in `plans/approved/2026-04-18-evelynn-memory-sharding.md`). Instead, write a new shard at `agents/evelynn/memory/last-sessions/<short-uuid>.md` where `<short-uuid>` is the UUID from Step 2's transcript path. Content: a structured 5–10 line handoff — date, session number, what happened, open threads, dangling commits or PRs, blockers. Stage:

```
git add agents/evelynn/memory/last-sessions/<short-uuid>.md
```

Note "remember:remember bypassed for evelynn — shard written to last-sessions/<short-uuid>.md" in the final report.

**If agent != evelynn:** Invoke the `remember:remember` skill via the Skill tool. This is the primary handoff mechanism — it writes `.remember/remember.md` with a structured snapshot of what is done, what is next, and any non-obvious context. The Remember plugin's `SessionStart` hook loads this automatically at the start of the next session.

```
Skill: remember:remember
```

Stage the output file:

```
git add .remember/remember.md
```

If the `remember` plugin is not installed or the skill is unavailable, fall back to writing `agents/<agent>/memory/last-session.md` manually with a 5–10 line terse handoff (date, what happened, open threads, dangling commits or PRs, blockers). Stage with `git add -f agents/<agent>/memory/last-session.md`. Note "remember step skipped — plugin not available, used last-session.md fallback" in the final report.

## Step 6b — Update open-threads.md + regenerate INDEX.md (coordinators only)

**Ordering invariant:** Step 6 (write shard) MUST complete before Step 6b because the shard is the source for both open-threads.md and INDEX.md updates. Step 6b MUST complete before Step 9 (commit + push) so all three artifacts land atomically in one commit.

**If agent is a coordinator (evelynn OR sona):** Run the following after Step 6 completes.

1. Parse the shard's `## Open threads into next session` section (or `## Open threads` section). For each thread listed:
   - If resolved/closed: remove or mark closed the matching `## <thread>` section in `agents/<agent>/memory/open-threads.md`.
   - If new or still-open: add or update its `## <thread>` section with the shard UUID as a pointer and a status one-liner.
   - You are the coordinator — you confirm the diff before writing. Hand-curation is the value here.
   - If `open-threads.md` does not exist yet, create it from scratch.

2. Stage:
   ```
   git add agents/<agent>/memory/open-threads.md
   ```

3. Regenerate `last-sessions/INDEX.md`:
   ```
   bash scripts/memory-consolidate.sh <agent> --index-only
   ```

4. Stage:
   ```
   git add agents/<agent>/memory/last-sessions/INDEX.md
   ```

If Step 6b fails partway (e.g., `--index-only` errors), the shard written in Step 6 is already staged and recoverable. Do NOT abort the session close — log the failure and proceed to Step 9 with only the shard staged. Recovery path: run `bash scripts/memory-consolidate.sh <agent> --index-only`, stage `INDEX.md`, and amend the next commit manually.

**If agent is NOT a coordinator (non-coordinator agents — Sonnet subagents, Lissandra standalone, etc.):** Step 6b is a no-op. Skip entirely and proceed to Step 7.

## Step 7 — Memory refresh

**If agent == evelynn:** Do NOT touch `agents/evelynn/memory/evelynn.md`. Instead, write a new shard at `agents/evelynn/memory/sessions/<short-uuid>.md` (same UUID from Step 2) containing:
- A `## Session YYYY-MM-DD (SN, <mode>)` heading.
- One-line summary of the session.
- Any delta notes to Key Context or Working Patterns that should be folded in at next consolidation.

Stage the shard:

```
git add agents/evelynn/memory/sessions/<short-uuid>.md
```

Note "evelynn memory shard written to sessions/<short-uuid>.md — consolidation will fold into evelynn.md at next boot" in the final report.

**If agent != evelynn:** Review `agents/<agent>/memory/<agent>.md`. If anything material changed this session (new working patterns, new known issues, sessions list), update it:

- Append a new session row to the `## Sessions` list with the format `- YYYY-MM-DD (SN, <mode>): <one-line summary>`.
- Prune stale entries if the file exceeds 50 lines. Remove the oldest session rows first.
- Update `## Key context` or `## Working patterns` only if the change is durable.

If nothing material changed, skip the update but still state "no memory changes this session" in the final report. Stage if modified:

```
git add agents/<agent>/memory/<agent>.md
```

## Step 8 — Learnings

If this session produced a generalizable lesson (something a future instance of this agent or a sibling agent would benefit from), write it to `agents/<agent>/learnings/<YYYY-MM-DD>-<topic>.md` and add a one-line reference to `agents/<agent>/learnings/index.md`.

If no learning, skip and state "no learnings this session" in the final report.

Stage any new learning files:

```
git add agents/<agent>/learnings/
```

## Step 9 — Commit + push

Build the commit message. Format:

```
chore: <agent> session closing — transcript, handoff, memory, learnings for YYYY-MM-DD <platform> session
```

Use `cli` as the platform for Claude Code sessions. Use HEREDOC form:

```
git commit -m "$(cat <<'EOF'
chore: <agent> session closing — transcript, handoff, memory, learnings for YYYY-MM-DD <platform> session

Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.6 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
EOF
)"
```

Then push:

```
git push
```

**If the pre-push hook rejects the commit** (wrong prefix, gitleaks hit, anything): STOP. Do not retry. Do not rewrite the commit. Report the error verbatim in the final report and exit with `end-session: commit rejected — manual intervention required`.

**If the push fails because main moved forward**: pull with merge (never rebase per CLAUDE.md git rules), then re-push. One retry only. If the second push fails, stop and report.

## Step 10 — Final report

Print a single-paragraph summary to the agent's output:

- Cleaned transcript path
- Commit hash
- Push status
- Journal / remember handoff / memory / learnings status (which were updated, which were skipped)
- Any warnings from the chain-walk or non-fatal errors along the way

Then exit. Do not close the session yourself — Duong or Evelynn explicitly ends the session after reviewing the report.

## Refusal posture

You are `disable-model-invocation: false`. This skill MUST only be triggered explicitly by Duong or Evelynn typing `/end-session`. It cannot auto-fire on model judgment. If Duong's intent is ambiguous, ask before firing.
