## Evelynn — 2026-04-22T06:31:44Z

Here's the detailed brief on each question. Swain's pick bolded.

---

**OQ-1: Severity floor for non-internal-prefix path misses** — **(a) info** / (b) warn / (c) keep block

*What it's about:* When a path-shaped backtick token (e.g. `POST /auth/session/{sid}` or `/foo/bar`) doesn't start with a known internal repo prefix, how loud should Orianna be when `test -e` misses?

*Why it matters:* Today, every path miss blocks — whether it's `scripts/real-file.sh` or an HTTP route. That conflation caused the 12-block firebase-auth run and the 10-block demo-studio run. Pick (a): HTTP routes become `info` — visible but non-blocking. Pick (c): authors keep manually suppressing every route.

*Risk of (a):* A genuine stale internal-path claim that accidentally looks like an HTTP route slips to info. Edge case; internal paths carry recognizable prefixes.

*Swain's reasoning:* `info` minimizes noise for the high-volume false-positive class while keeping block for the class that's caught real defects.

---

**OQ-2: Fenced-block extraction** — **(a) hard drop** / (b) drop + opt-in re-enable marker / (c) keep with expanded allowlist

*What it's about:* Should Orianna stop extracting path tokens from fenced code blocks entirely, or let authors mark individual fences for checking?

*Why it matters:* Fenced blocks are diagrams, pseudocode, example shell sessions — almost never genuine unresolved file claims. (a) removes extraction entirely. (b) adds opt-in `<!-- orianna: check -->` marker. (c) keeps extraction with more allowlist entries — the exact treadmill we're trying to exit.

*Risk of (a):* A stale path appearing only inside a fence isn't caught. Swain's audit shows zero documented cases; the same path is always cited in prose elsewhere too.

*Swain's reasoning:* Adding a second marker syntax doubles cognitive overhead; the failure mode is too-much-extraction, so simpler-cut is cleanest.

---

**OQ-3: TG-2/3/4 estimate_minutes validation** — **(a) drop from Orianna** / (b) keep deprecated then delete / (c) keep as redundancy

*What it's about:* Orianna verifies `estimate_minutes` integer/range/units at sign-time. The pre-commit linter runs the same checks at commit-time. Drop Orianna's copies?

*Why it matters:* (a) makes the linter sole owner — fast feedback at commit, no redundant LLM spend at promote. (b) keeps Orianna's copies marked deprecated, removed later. (c) both enforce in parallel, adding sign-time LLM tokens for no additional safety.

*Risk of (a):* If the linter ever regresses, Orianna no longer backstops. Swain judges acceptable — linter has its own test coverage.

*Swain's reasoning:* Linter is strictly upstream of Orianna; re-running at promote time is tautological and burns sign-time budget.

---

**OQ-4: Step-A frontmatter checks (`status:`, `created:`, `tags:`)** — **(a) warn** / (b) drop entirely / (c) keep as block

*What it's about:* These fields are already enforced by the pre-commit linter. Should Orianna demote to warn, drop entirely, or keep as block?

*Why it matters:* (a) keeps non-blocking visibility — cheap linter-regression canary. (b) removes Orianna's copies entirely, single authority with linter. (c) contradicts the substance-vs-format directive — these are format fields, not correctness.

*Risk of (a):* Minor visual noise in reports. Practical cost is tiny since they never block.

*Swain's reasoning:* Free non-blocking signal is worth keeping; overhead is a report line, not an iteration loop.

---

**OQ-5: Sequencing vs `orianna-gate-speedups`** — **(a) this plan first** / (b) parallel / (c) speedups first ⚠️ *conflict with my in-flight Viktor dispatch*

*What it's about:* Both plans target the same gate from different angles — rescope shrinks the check set, speedups optimizes ceremony around the current check set.

*Why it matters:* (a) rescope first → speedups implementer measures whether the originally-scoped optimizations are still needed at the reduced scope (might be over-engineering). (b) parallel — feasible since different files, but speedups may over-engineer. (c) speedups first — invests in ceremony that may become unnecessary.

*Risk of (a):* Speedups progress pauses until this plan approves + ships. If this plan stalls, speedups stall too.

*Swain's reasoning:* Measuring post-rescope iteration count before committing to full speedups scope avoids optimizing a problem that's already been substantially reduced.

**Status:** I dispatched Viktor on speedups earlier. If you pick (a), I pause Viktor now.

---

**OQ-6: Claim-contract version bump** — (a) bump in place / **(b) bump + v1→v2 delta note** / (c) archive v1 alongside

*What it's about:* `claim-contract.md` bumps from v1 to v2. Update the version number only, add an inline delta paragraph, or keep a full archived v1 file?

*Why it matters:* (a) relies on `git log` for history — minimal but requires reader to dig. (b) adds a short delta section at the top explaining what changed — future agents immediately see why v2 extracts less. (c) preserves complete v1 text as a second file — ongoing maintenance of two files.

*Risk of (b):* A poorly-written delta note could go stale. Low risk since changes are well-defined.

*Swain's reasoning:* Future agents will encounter v2's shrunken extraction heuristic; a delta paragraph is a cheap durability investment vs sending them to git log.

---

Compact answer: `1a 2a 3a 4a 5? 6b`. Skip = concur.

## Duong — 2026-04-22T07:45:58Z

Base directory for this skill: /Users/duongntd99/Documents/Personal/strawberry-agents/.claude/skills/pre-compact-save

# /pre-compact-save — Pre-Compact Memory Consolidation

## When to use

- Before running `/compact` on an Evelynn or Sona coordinator session
- When the PreCompact hook blocks `/compact` and asks you to consolidate first
- When you want a mid-session snapshot without ending the session

## When NOT to use

- Subagent sessions (out of scope — Lissandra only handles coordinator sessions)
- Actual session end (use `/end-session` instead — it produces the full transcript archive)
- Immediately after a recent consolidation (redundant; worst case it produces a duplicate)

## Arguments

`` (optional): `evelynn` or `sona` to override auto-detection. Empty → auto-detect from session greeting.

## Protocol

1. **Preflight.**
   - Read the session jsonl path: `~/.claude/projects/<project-slug>/<session-id>.jsonl`. Derive `session_id` and `transcript_path` from the current environment.
   - If `` is non-empty, use it as the coordinator. Otherwise detect:
     - Scan the first 3 user messages for `Hey Sona` (case-insensitive) → coordinator = `sona`
     - Otherwise coordinator = `evelynn` (repo default per CLAUDE.md Caller Routing)
   - Cross-check `[concern: work]` vs `[concern: personal]` tags on subagent prompts. Contradiction → refuse with a diagnostic.

2. **Spawn Lissandra** via the Agent tool with `subagent_type: "Lissandra"`. Note: Lissandra updates `open-threads.md` and regenerates `INDEX.md` as part of the coordinator shard write, same as `/end-session` Step 6b. Prompt shape:

   ```
   [concern: <personal|work>]

   Consolidate this coordinator session before /compact. You are impersonating <coordinator>.

   - session_id: <uuid>
   - transcript_path: <absolute path to jsonl>
   - coordinator: <evelynn|sona>

   Run the full protocol in your agent definition (handoff shard, session shard, conditional learnings, journal entry, optional transcript excerpt, commit, sentinel). Write to `agents/<coordinator>/...` directories only. Use the coordinator's first-person voice.

   Report back with: artifact paths, commit SHA, push status, skipped steps (if any), warnings.
   ```

3. **On Lissandra return:**
   - Verify the sentinel file exists at `/tmp/claude-precompact-saved-<session_id>`. If not, report failure and exit — the PreCompact hook will still block on next `/compact`.
   - Verify the commit landed on main. `git log -1 --format='%H %s'` should show Lissandra's consolidation commit.
   - Report the artifact paths + commit SHA back to the coordinator.

4. **Done.** Coordinator can now safely run `/compact`; the PreCompact hook will see the sentinel and allow compaction.

## Failure modes

- **Coordinator detection contradiction** — refuse, surface the inconsistency. Duong resolves manually by supplying ``.
- **Lissandra commit rejected by pre-push hook** — Lissandra reports verbatim. Do not retry; let Duong diagnose.
- **No sentinel after Lissandra return** — indicates Lissandra's final step didn't fire. Report and exit without touching the sentinel ourselves (the sentinel is Lissandra's signature that she completed).

## What this skill does NOT do

- Does not run `/end-session`. That skill is `disable-model-invocation: true` for a reason.
- Does not compact. You still run `/compact` yourself after this skill succeeds.
- Does not archive the full session transcript. That is end-session's job.

## Duong — 2026-04-22T07:54:18Z

what happend with Ekko? Why does it need me to bypass?

## Evelynn — 2026-04-22T07:54:38Z

**What Ekko hit — the chain:**

Both plans (STAGED_SCOPE + inbox-watch) were already at `in-progress/` with valid `approved` + `in_progress` signatures. To promote to `implemented/`, Orianna's **implementation-gate** (newly tightened in the speedups work) checks:
- **Block B:** frontmatter has `architecture_changes:` or `architecture_impact:`
- **Block C:** body has a `## Test results` section

Both plans were authored before those checks existed, so both fail.

**The trap:** Adding Block C (`## Test results`) modifies the plan body → **body-hash changes** → prior signatures become invalid → you must re-sign the whole chain from scratch (`proposed → approved → in_progress → implemented`). This works fine when the re-sign chain is clean.

**Why Plan 1 (STAGED_SCOPE) needs a bypass:**
Earlier today someone (Duong) committed a `chore: test commit` + `Revert "chore: test commit"` pair (`c87614d` / `c6a1743`) that touched the `orianna_signature_approved:` line of the staged-scope plan directly. `orianna-verify-signature.sh` walks git log newest→oldest and treats the *most recent commit to touch the signature field* as the signing commit. That commit is now the revert — authored by `Duongntd`, not the Orianna script identity — so the verifier rejects it as "wrong author email." 

Re-signing can't fix it because the contamination is baked into history. Only way forward: commit the `implemented` promotion with an `Orianna-Bypass:` trailer, which **per Rule 19 is valid only when the commit author is `harukainguyen1411`** (your admin identity). Agents are explicitly rejected by the pre-commit hook if they try.

**Plan 2 (inbox-watch) does NOT need a bypass** — no contamination. Ekko stopped because it hit the same body-fix re-sign treadmill simultaneously on both plans and wanted human signoff before drilling further. Option B in Ekko's report (clean re-sign, no bypass) works for inbox-watch alone.

**TL;DR:** Git-log contamination from an old test/revert pair makes the automated signature-verifier believe you, personally, signed the plan under the wrong identity — unfixable in history. Bypass trailer under admin identity is the only escape hatch, and by design only you can issue it.

## Duong — 2026-04-22T07:55:50Z

so this happens because we updated the orianna check during the implemtation of Ekko's? This is one time?

## Evelynn — 2026-04-22T07:56:07Z

**Mostly yes — one-time migration hazard, two distinct issues:**

**1. Body-hash / `## Test results` + `architecture_changes:` requirement — one-time backfill pain.**
The speedups PR #19 (merged today) tightened Orianna's implementation-gate to require those fields. Plans that were already at `in-progress/` before this landed didn't have them, so any `→ implemented` promotion now forces a body edit → full re-sign chain. Once a plan ships through the new gate end-to-end, it's fine. Future plans will be written with these fields from day one, so they won't hit this.

**Affected plans:** just the ones currently sitting in `in-progress/` authored before today — staged-scope, inbox-watch, and anything else you find when sweeping. Small finite set. After they clear, this class of pain is gone.

**2. Git-log contamination on staged-scope — one-time accident, not a gate change.**
The `chore: test commit` + `Revert "chore: test commit"` pair earlier today touched the `orianna_signature_approved:` field of the staged-scope plan. The verifier treats the newest commit that modified the field as "the signing commit" and checks its author. The revert was authored by you (`Duongntd`, not the Orianna-script identity) → verifier rejects. This is not caused by the gate change; it's collateral from a manual test commit. Won't happen again unless another test/revert touches a signature field.

**So: yes, one-time.** Going forward:
- New plans authored under the current Orianna version include `## Test results` + `architecture_changes:` from the start → no re-sign treadmill.
- No more test/revert commits on signature fields → no contamination.

The fast-follow plan (in-progress now) will clean up the residual stricter-than-intended hooks (Senna F1/F2/F3 + Ekko's `pre-commit-t-plan-structure.sh` bare-match finding), further reducing false blocks.

## Duong — 2026-04-22T07:59:16Z

the error error: An unknown error occurred, possibly due to low max file descriptors (Unexpected)

Current limit: 256

To fix this, try running:

  ulimit -n 2147483646

If that still doesn't work, you may need to run:

  sudo launchctl limit maxfiles 2147483646
duongntd99@Duongs-MacBook-Pro-2 strawberry-agents % again. how to fix this

## Evelynn — 2026-04-22T07:59:39Z

**Canonical macOS fix (permanent, survives reboot):**

**1. System-level (kernel limits — requires sudo, one-time):**

Create `/Library/LaunchDaemons/limit.maxfiles.plist`:

```bash
sudo tee /Library/LaunchDaemons/limit.maxfiles.plist > /dev/null <<'EOF'
<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?>
<!DOCTYPE plist PUBLIC "-//Apple//DTD PLIST 1.0//EN" "http://www.apple.com/DTDs/PropertyList-1.0.dtd">
<plist version="1.0">
  <dict>
    <key>Label</key><string>limit.maxfiles</string>
    <key>ProgramArguments</key>
    <array>
      <string>launchctl</string><string>limit</string><string>maxfiles</string>
      <string>524288</string><string>524288</string>
    </array>
    <key>RunAtLoad</key><true/>
    <key>ServiceIPC</key><false/>
  </dict>
</plist>
EOF
sudo chown root:wheel /Library/LaunchDaemons/limit.maxfiles.plist
sudo chmod 644 /Library/LaunchDaemons/limit.maxfiles.plist
sudo launchctl load -w /Library/LaunchDaemons/limit.maxfiles.plist
```

**2. Shell-level (per-session, add to `~/.zshrc`):**

```bash
echo 'ulimit -n 65536' >> ~/.zshrc
source ~/.zshrc
```

**3. Verify:**

```bash
launchctl limit maxfiles        # should show 524288 524288
ulimit -n                       # should show 65536 (or higher)
```

**4. Immediate fix for the current terminal (no reboot needed):**

```bash
ulimit -n 65536
```

Then re-run whatever failed. 524288 is Apple's current sane max; don't use `2147483646` (that's INT_MAX, macOS silently caps it and sometimes wedges).

**Why this keeps happening to you:** Claude Code spawns many parallel subagent processes; each holds file descriptors for the transcript jsonl, socket, and tool I/O. A fresh macOS shell is 256, which burns through fast once 3–5 agents run concurrently. Once you set step 1+2, it's permanent.

**Also:** your working directory vanished from the shell (I got a "directory no longer exists" error just now). After raising the limit, `cd ~/Documents/Personal/strawberry-agents` before resuming.

/Users/duongntd99/.zshrc:source:24: operation not permitted: /Users/duongntd99/Documents/Personal/strawberry-agents/scripts/mac/aliases.sh
duongntd99@Duongs-MacBook-Pro-2 mmp % my iterm is broken. I'm on normal termnial

## Evelynn — 2026-04-22T08:08:25Z

"Operation not permitted" on source ≠ permissions — it's macOS TCC (Transparency/Consent/Control). Terminal.app doesn't have the disk-access entitlement that iTerm did.

**Two fixes, in order of likelihood:**

**1. Grant Terminal.app Full Disk Access** (most likely cause):
- System Settings → Privacy & Security → **Full Disk Access**
- Click `+`, add `/Applications/Utilities/Terminal.app`
- Restart Terminal (fully quit: ⌘Q)

Also check **Files and Folders** and **Developer Tools** in the same Privacy pane — grant Terminal access there if listed.

**2. If that's not it, check quarantine xattr on the file:**
```bash
xattr -l /Users/duongntd99/Documents/Personal/strawberry-agents/scripts/mac/aliases.sh
```
If you see `com.apple.quarantine`, strip it:
```bash
xattr -d com.apple.quarantine /Users/duongntd99/Documents/Personal/strawberry-agents/scripts/mac/aliases.sh
```

**3. Fix iTerm while you're at it** — iTerm likely lost its TCC grants after a macOS update. Same Full Disk Access pane, remove + re-add `iTerm.app`. If iTerm crashes on launch, reinstall from iterm2.com (preserves prefs).

**Meanwhile** you can bypass the broken line by commenting out line 24 of `~/.zshrc` temporarily, or running `source ~/.zshrc 2>/dev/null` to suppress the error — the rest of the rc will still load.

```bash
open -a iTerm --args --disable-unified-clipboard
```
Inside iTerm, if still hung, type nothing — just ⌘, (comma) to open Prefs → **Profiles** → **Default** → **General** → **Command** → pick **Custom Shell** → set to `/bin/zsh -f` → close prefs → ⌘T for new tab.

Relaunch iTerm. You lose customization but it will definitely start clean.

## Duong — 2026-04-22T08:37:51Z

code.iterm2.plist.bak
duongntd99@Duongs-MacBook-Pro-2 mmp % ps aux | grep iTerm2 | grep -v grep
duongntd99       53587  91.9  0.0 412013280    352   ??  R     3:37PM   0:12.41 /Applications/iTerm.app/Contents/MacOS/iTerm2
duongntd99@Duongs-MacBook-Pro-2 mmp %

## Evelynn — 2026-04-22T08:38:31Z

**Root cause found — and it's our own fix backfiring.**

iTerm's `iTermExec` does a naive `close()` loop over all FDs up to the hard limit before spawning each shell. We raised `launchctl maxfiles` to **524288** this afternoon — so iTerm is now calling `close(fd)` 524288 times in a kernel-tight loop per spawn. 2454/2514 samples are literally in `close()`. That's your 96% CPU spin.

**Fix:** lower the launchctl ceiling to something sane. 65536 is fine (your shell already has that).

## Evelynn — 2026-04-22T08:38:47Z

Live limit is actually **2147483646** (INT_MAX) — even worse. iTerm's close-loop is doing ~2 billion iterations per shell spawn. That's literally unkillable-spin territory.

Run these in Terminal (needs sudo):

```bash
sudo launchctl limit maxfiles 65536 65536
sudo sed -i '' 's/524288/65536/g' /Library/LaunchDaemons/limit.maxfiles.plist
sudo launchctl unload /Library/LaunchDaemons/limit.maxfiles.plist
sudo launchctl load -w /Library/LaunchDaemons/limit.maxfiles.plist
launchctl limit maxfiles
```

Last line should print `maxfiles 65536 65536`. Then:

```bash
open -a iTerm
```

iTerm should start instantly — close-loop is now 65k iterations instead of 2 billion. Your shell's `ulimit -n 65536` from `.zshrc` is already well-aligned with this.

**Bottom line: you don't need a 524k FD limit, let alone INT_MAX. 65536 is plenty for Claude Code + MCP servers.** This is the #1 lesson — learned today. I'll note it for the inbox/cwd-wedge learning.

## Evelynn — 2026-04-22T08:40:05Z

SIP is blocking runtime changes — the plist edit will only take effect after a reboot. But we can launch iTerm with a lower FD limit directly from a shell (bypassing launchd inheritance):

## Evelynn — 2026-04-22T08:40:21Z

Shell inherits `unlimited` too — that's the source of iTerm's pain whether launched from shell or Finder. Drop it and launch iTerm directly (bypass `open`/LaunchServices, which would re-inherit the unlimited ceiling):

```bash
ulimit -n 1024
ulimit -Hn 1024
/Applications/iTerm.app/Contents/MacOS/iTerm2 &
disown
```

That forks iTerm as a child of your shell with the 1024 ceiling. iTerm's close-loop will run 1024 iterations instead of 2 billion — should start instantly.

**Permanent fix requires reboot.** The plist is already edited to 65536; after reboot, launchd's own limit will be 65536 and everything it spawns (iTerm, Claude Code, etc.) inherits that.

**After reboot, verify:**
```bash
launchctl limit maxfiles
```
Should show `65536 65536`. If it still shows INT_MAX:
```bash
cat /Library/LaunchDaemons/limit.maxfiles.plist | grep -E '524288|65536'
```
Should show `65536` only.

## Duong — 2026-04-22T08:53:01Z

how can I apply another profile to this iterm?

## Evelynn — 2026-04-22T08:53:13Z

You can restore the backup or pick a new default:

**Restore your previous profile (full settings):**
```bash
killall iTerm2
mv ~/Library/Preferences/com.googlecode.iterm2.plist.bak ~/Library/Preferences/com.googlecode.iterm2.plist
killall cfprefsd
open -a iTerm
```
Brings back all your old profiles, shortcuts, color schemes.

**Or apply a profile while iTerm is running:**
- **Per window:** iTerm menu → **Profiles** → pick one. That window switches.
- **Make default:** ⌘, (Prefs) → **Profiles** tab → select the profile → **Other Actions** (gear icon at bottom-left) → **Set as Default**.

**Import a profile from a file (e.g. `.itermcolors` or `.json` export):**
- ⌘, → **Profiles** → **Other Actions** → **Import JSON Profiles…** (for full profile)
- Or **Colors** tab → **Color Presets…** → **Import…** (for color-only `.itermcolors` files)

**Create fresh from a preset** (Solarized, Dracula, etc.):
- ⌘, → **Profiles** → `+` → configure → **Colors** → **Color Presets** dropdown → pick.

If you lost custom profiles when we nuked the plist and just want them back, option 1 is what you want.

## Duong — 2026-04-22T08:54:06Z

no, I just want this wondow/session to use a dynamic profile I already setup. Can can launch a new window but then I would have to close this one

## Evelynn — 2026-04-22T08:54:16Z

In iTerm's menu bar: **Session → Change Profile → [pick your dynamic profile]**

That swaps the profile on the *current* session only — no new window, no close. The session retains its shell state (history, cwd, running processes), just re-applies colors/keybinds/fonts/env from the new profile.

If you want it as a shortcut: ⌘, → **Keys** → **Key Bindings** → `+` → action **"Change Profile"** → pick a key.

Alternative one-off: ⌘I (**Edit Session…**) lets you override individual settings for just this session without switching profile.

Base directory for this skill: /Users/duongntd99/Documents/Personal/strawberry-agents/.claude/skills/pre-compact-save

# /pre-compact-save — Pre-Compact Memory Consolidation

## When to use

- Before running `/compact` on an Evelynn or Sona coordinator session
- When the PreCompact hook blocks `/compact` and asks you to consolidate first
- When you want a mid-session snapshot without ending the session

## When NOT to use

- Subagent sessions (out of scope — Lissandra only handles coordinator sessions)
- Actual session end (use `/end-session` instead — it produces the full transcript archive)
- Immediately after a recent consolidation (redundant; worst case it produces a duplicate)

## Arguments

`` (optional): `evelynn` or `sona` to override auto-detection. Empty → auto-detect from session greeting.

## Protocol

1. **Preflight.**
   - Read the session jsonl path: `~/.claude/projects/<project-slug>/<session-id>.jsonl`. Derive `session_id` and `transcript_path` from the current environment.
   - If `` is non-empty, use it as the coordinator. Otherwise detect:
     - Scan the first 3 user messages for `Hey Sona` (case-insensitive) → coordinator = `sona`
     - Otherwise coordinator = `evelynn` (repo default per CLAUDE.md Caller Routing)
   - Cross-check `[concern: work]` vs `[concern: personal]` tags on subagent prompts. Contradiction → refuse with a diagnostic.

2. **Spawn Lissandra** via the Agent tool with `subagent_type: "Lissandra"`. Note: Lissandra updates `open-threads.md` and regenerates `INDEX.md` as part of the coordinator shard write, same as `/end-session` Step 6b. Prompt shape:

   ```
   [concern: <personal|work>]

   Consolidate this coordinator session before /compact. You are impersonating <coordinator>.

   - session_id: <uuid>
   - transcript_path: <absolute path to jsonl>
   - coordinator: <evelynn|sona>

   Run the full protocol in your agent definition (handoff shard, session shard, conditional learnings, journal entry, optional transcript excerpt, commit, sentinel). Write to `agents/<coordinator>/...` directories only. Use the coordinator's first-person voice.

   Report back with: artifact paths, commit SHA, push status, skipped steps (if any), warnings.
   ```

3. **On Lissandra return:**
   - Verify the sentinel file exists at `/tmp/claude-precompact-saved-<session_id>`. If not, report failure and exit — the PreCompact hook will still block on next `/compact`.
   - Verify the commit landed on main. `git log -1 --format='%H %s'` should show Lissandra's consolidation commit.
   - Report the artifact paths + commit SHA back to the coordinator.

4. **Done.** Coordinator can now safely run `/compact`; the PreCompact hook will see the sentinel and allow compaction.

## Failure modes

- **Coordinator detection contradiction** — refuse, surface the inconsistency. Duong resolves manually by supplying ``.
- **Lissandra commit rejected by pre-push hook** — Lissandra reports verbatim. Do not retry; let Duong diagnose.
- **No sentinel after Lissandra return** — indicates Lissandra's final step didn't fire. Report and exit without touching the sentinel ourselves (the sentinel is Lissandra's signature that she completed).

## What this skill does NOT do

- Does not run `/end-session`. That skill is `disable-model-invocation: true` for a reason.
- Does not compact. You still run `/compact` yourself after this skill succeeds.
- Does not archive the full session transcript. That is end-session's job.

## Evelynn — 2026-04-22T09:59:38Z

Short answer: **safe in principle, but not in this worktree yet.**

The fix (`flock`-based shared lock via `git rev-parse --git-common-dir`) landed on `origin/main` as `94c65ca`. Once that's in your local main worktree filesystem, both coordinators use it automatically — scripts are re-read on every invocation, so **no agent restart, no iTerm restart needed**.

**The gap right now:** `git pull --ff-only` refused because local main has diverged / has uncommitted state. So this worktree is still running the pre-fix `orianna-sign.sh` and has no `_lib_coordinator_lock.sh`. If Sona does a promote/sign from here concurrently with me, we're back to the old race.

**To close the gap, pick one:**

1. **Cleanest:** commit or stash the untracked pile (screenshots, learnings, `.no-precompact-save`), then `git pull --ff-only`. Both sessions immediately pick up the lock.
2. **Quickest:** just be aware that until (1) happens, don't run promote/sign in parallel between Evelynn and Sona.

Also worth knowing: the lock's shared state is `.git/strawberry-promote.lock` resolved via `--git-common-dir`, so it coordinates across worktrees — Evelynn and Sona running from different worktrees is fine once the fix is in each worktree's filesystem.

**No restart needed.** Scripts are re-read every invocation; the lock uses `.git/strawberry-promote.lock` via `git rev-parse --git-common-dir` so it serializes Evelynn vs Sona regardless of which worktree each operates from. If both hit a promote/sign at once, one gets the lock, the other fast-fails with a PID-labeled "coordinator is already running" message instead of racing.

Base directory for this skill: /Users/duongntd99/Documents/Personal/strawberry-agents/.claude/skills/pre-compact-save

# /pre-compact-save — Pre-Compact Memory Consolidation

## When to use

- Before running `/compact` on an Evelynn or Sona coordinator session
- When the PreCompact hook blocks `/compact` and asks you to consolidate first
- When you want a mid-session snapshot without ending the session

## When NOT to use

- Subagent sessions (out of scope — Lissandra only handles coordinator sessions)
- Actual session end (use `/end-session` instead — it produces the full transcript archive)
- Immediately after a recent consolidation (redundant; worst case it produces a duplicate)

## Arguments

`` (optional): `evelynn` or `sona` to override auto-detection. Empty → auto-detect from session greeting.

## Protocol

1. **Preflight.**
   - Read the session jsonl path: `~/.claude/projects/<project-slug>/<session-id>.jsonl`. Derive `session_id` and `transcript_path` from the current environment.
   - If `` is non-empty, use it as the coordinator. Otherwise detect:
     - Scan the first 3 user messages for `Hey Sona` (case-insensitive) → coordinator = `sona`
     - Otherwise coordinator = `evelynn` (repo default per CLAUDE.md Caller Routing)
   - Cross-check `[concern: work]` vs `[concern: personal]` tags on subagent prompts. Contradiction → refuse with a diagnostic.

2. **Spawn Lissandra** via the Agent tool with `subagent_type: "Lissandra"`. Note: Lissandra updates `open-threads.md` and regenerates `INDEX.md` as part of the coordinator shard write, same as `/end-session` Step 6b. Prompt shape:

   ```
   [concern: <personal|work>]

   Consolidate this coordinator session before /compact. You are impersonating <coordinator>.

   - session_id: <uuid>
   - transcript_path: <absolute path to jsonl>
   - coordinator: <evelynn|sona>

   Run the full protocol in your agent definition (handoff shard, session shard, conditional learnings, journal entry, optional transcript excerpt, commit, sentinel). Write to `agents/<coordinator>/...` directories only. Use the coordinator's first-person voice.

   Report back with: artifact paths, commit SHA, push status, skipped steps (if any), warnings.
   ```

3. **On Lissandra return:**
   - Verify the sentinel file exists at `/tmp/claude-precompact-saved-<session_id>`. If not, report failure and exit — the PreCompact hook will still block on next `/compact`.
   - Verify the commit landed on main. `git log -1 --format='%H %s'` should show Lissandra's consolidation commit.
   - Report the artifact paths + commit SHA back to the coordinator.

4. **Done.** Coordinator can now safely run `/compact`; the PreCompact hook will see the sentinel and allow compaction.

## Failure modes

- **Coordinator detection contradiction** — refuse, surface the inconsistency. Duong resolves manually by supplying ``.
- **Lissandra commit rejected by pre-push hook** — Lissandra reports verbatim. Do not retry; let Duong diagnose.
- **No sentinel after Lissandra return** — indicates Lissandra's final step didn't fire. Report and exit without touching the sentinel ourselves (the sentinel is Lissandra's signature that she completed).

## What this skill does NOT do

- Does not run `/end-session`. That skill is `disable-model-invocation: true` for a reason.
- Does not compact. You still run `/compact` yourself after this skill succeeds.
- Does not archive the full session transcript. That is end-session's job.

2. Key Technical Concepts:
   - Rule 18 self-merge amendment: agent can merge own-authored PR when (a) required checks green, (b) non-author approval present, (c) no --admin bypass. Dropped the author-is-not-merger clause.
   - Rule 16 strengthening: name Akali explicitly, require Playwright MCP, extend trigger to "UI or user flow."
   - Work-scope reviewer anonymity: deny agent names, github handles, emails in work-scope reviews/comments/commits; pre-commit + reviewer-auth.sh pre-submit enforcement.
   - Canonical scope-detection signal: `git remote get-url origin` regex match on `[:/]missmp/`.
   - Coordinator lock (flock via `git rev-parse --git-common-dir` → `.git/strawberry-promote.lock`) serializes Evelynn+Sona concurrent promote/sign.
   - Monitor-based inbox watcher (strawberry-inbox-channel v3) watches gitignored agents/<coord>/inbox/ directory.
   - Orianna implementation-gate check requires `architecture_changes:` or `architecture_impact: none` + body section, AND `## Test results` section.
   - Body-hash signature invalidation treadmill: editing plan body after signing requires re-sign through full proposed → approved → in_progress chain.
   - Rule 12 (xfail-first TDD): xfail test commit must precede impl commit on-branch.
   - Rule 11 (no git rebase, always merge).
   - Rule 19 (Orianna-Bypass trailer admin-only under harukainguyen1411 identity).
   - Dual reviewer accounts: strawberry-reviewers (Lucian), strawberry-reviewers-2 (Senna).
   - Fabrication detector in orianna-sign.sh blocks fake test results.
   - Claude API auth expiry mid-subagent-run → resume path.

## Duong — 2026-04-22T11:30:00Z

how can I disable email notification from github?

## Evelynn — 2026-04-22T11:30:12Z

GitHub notification settings for email:

**Global toggle:** https://github.com/settings/notifications — turn off the "Email" column checkboxes for what you don't want (Participating, Watching, etc.).

**Per-repo watch level:** https://github.com/harukainguyen1411/strawberry-agents — top-right "Watch" button → "Custom" or "Ignore" / "Participating and @mentions only" to stop review/comment noise.

**Nuke Actions emails specifically:** https://github.com/settings/notifications → scroll to "Actions" → uncheck "Send notifications for failed workflows only" + any Email box there.

**Filter inbox side:** Gmail filter on `from:notifications@github.com` → Skip Inbox + Label. Keeps a record without pinging you.

Most common fix for agent-heavy repos: Watch level → "Participating and @mentions only" on the strawberry-agents repo. That stops the per-PR/per-review flood but keeps @mentions if anyone tags you directly.

## Evelynn — 2026-04-22T11:32:28Z

The email is going to the **`strawberry-reviewers`** account (see email headers: `to harukainguyen1411/strawberry-agents, strawberry-reviewers, Review`), not your primary `harukainguyen1411` account. The settings you changed are only for the primary account.

**Fix:** log into the `strawberry-reviewers` and `strawberry-reviewers-2` GitHub accounts separately and change their notification settings too. Same page — https://github.com/settings/notifications — but while signed in as each reviewer identity.

Those two accounts are the ones being @-review-requested by the agent system, so GitHub fires "review requested" emails to *their* registered email addresses. If those addresses happen to be aliases to your inbox (common pattern with `+strawberry-reviewers@gmail.com` or similar Gmail aliasing), you'll keep getting them until you silence them at the source account.

Two options:
1. Disable Participating email on both reviewer accounts (via their own /settings/notifications).
2. Point those accounts' notification email to a throwaway/blackhole address (no-reply like). Safer, since you won't miss genuine @-mentions on your primary.

Base directory for this skill: /Users/duongntd99/Documents/Personal/strawberry-agents/.claude/skills/pre-compact-save

# /pre-compact-save — Pre-Compact Memory Consolidation

## When to use

- Before running `/compact` on an Evelynn or Sona coordinator session
- When the PreCompact hook blocks `/compact` and asks you to consolidate first
- When you want a mid-session snapshot without ending the session

## When NOT to use

- Subagent sessions (out of scope — Lissandra only handles coordinator sessions)
- Actual session end (use `/end-session` instead — it produces the full transcript archive)
- Immediately after a recent consolidation (redundant; worst case it produces a duplicate)

## Arguments

`` (optional): `evelynn` or `sona` to override auto-detection. Empty → auto-detect from session greeting.

## Protocol

1. **Preflight.**
   - Read the session jsonl path: `~/.claude/projects/<project-slug>/<session-id>.jsonl`. Derive `session_id` and `transcript_path` from the current environment.
   - If `` is non-empty, use it as the coordinator. Otherwise detect:
     - Scan the first 3 user messages for `Hey Sona` (case-insensitive) → coordinator = `sona`
     - Otherwise coordinator = `evelynn` (repo default per CLAUDE.md Caller Routing)
   - Cross-check `[concern: work]` vs `[concern: personal]` tags on subagent prompts. Contradiction → refuse with a diagnostic.

2. **Spawn Lissandra** via the Agent tool with `subagent_type: "Lissandra"`. Note: Lissandra updates `open-threads.md` and regenerates `INDEX.md` as part of the coordinator shard write, same as `/end-session` Step 6b. Prompt shape:

   ```
   [concern: <personal|work>]

   Consolidate this coordinator session before /compact. You are impersonating <coordinator>.

   - session_id: <uuid>
   - transcript_path: <absolute path to jsonl>
   - coordinator: <evelynn|sona>

   Run the full protocol in your agent definition (handoff shard, session shard, conditional learnings, journal entry, optional transcript excerpt, commit, sentinel). Write to `agents/<coordinator>/...` directories only. Use the coordinator's first-person voice.

   Report back with: artifact paths, commit SHA, push status, skipped steps (if any), warnings.
   ```

3. **On Lissandra return:**
   - Verify the sentinel file exists at `/tmp/claude-precompact-saved-<session_id>`. If not, report failure and exit — the PreCompact hook will still block on next `/compact`.
   - Verify the commit landed on main. `git log -1 --format='%H %s'` should show Lissandra's consolidation commit.
   - Report the artifact paths + commit SHA back to the coordinator.

4. **Done.** Coordinator can now safely run `/compact`; the PreCompact hook will see the sentinel and allow compaction.

## Failure modes

- **Coordinator detection contradiction** — refuse, surface the inconsistency. Duong resolves manually by supplying ``.
- **Lissandra commit rejected by pre-push hook** — Lissandra reports verbatim. Do not retry; let Duong diagnose.
- **No sentinel after Lissandra return** — indicates Lissandra's final step didn't fire. Report and exit without touching the sentinel ourselves (the sentinel is Lissandra's signature that she completed).

## What this skill does NOT do

- Does not run `/end-session`. That skill is `disable-model-invocation: true` for a reason.
- Does not compact. You still run `/compact` yourself after this skill succeeds.
- Does not archive the full session transcript. That is end-session's job.

## Duong — 2026-04-22T17:08:41Z

Base directory for this skill: /Users/duongntd99/Documents/Personal/strawberry-agents/.claude/skills/end-session

# /end-session — top-level session close

You are closing a top-level Claude Code session. This skill wraps the full close-session protocol into a deterministic checklist. Follow every step in order. Do not skip steps. Do not reorder.

## Argument

`` is the agent name whose session is being closed. If empty, refuse immediately with `end-session: agent name required — pass the agent name as an argument (e.g. /end-session evelynn)` and exit. If `` is set to something other than a valid agent name (no matching `agents/<name>/` directory), refuse with `end-session: unknown agent <name>` and exit.

## Step 0 — Context probe

Run these Bash commands in a single call and keep the output in mind:

```
pwd
git status --short
git log -1 --oneline
date -u +%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%SZ
```

If the working tree has uncommitted changes unrelated to the session close (files outside `agents/<agent>/`, `scripts/`, `CLAUDE.md`, `.gitignore`), stop and report: `end-session: working tree dirty with unrelated files — commit or stash before closing`. Do not proceed.

## Step 1 — Discover source jsonl

Run the cleaner in dry-run mode (just discovery, no write) using the Bash tool:

```
python scripts/clean-jsonl.py --agent <agent> --session auto --out /tmp/end-session-probe.md
```

Note: for Phase 1, the cleaner does not have a separate dry-run flag. The `/tmp/` output path is a throwaway probe. After the probe, delete `/tmp/end-session-probe.md`.

Capture the stderr for any `CLEANER: chain ambiguous` warnings and relay them to the agent for confirmation before proceeding.

## Step 2 — Clean transcript

Run the cleaner for real:

```
python scripts/clean-jsonl.py --agent <agent> --session auto
```

The cleaner writes to the default path `agents/<agent>/transcripts/<YYYY-MM-DD>-<short-uuid>.md`.

- On exit code 0: record the output path from the cleaner's stdout.
- On exit code 1: report the error and stop. Do not proceed to any further step.
- On exit code 2: report the internal error and stop.
- On exit code 3: report the secret match verbatim, STOP IMMEDIATELY, do not stage any files, do not run the commit step. Escalate to Duong via the final report.

## Step 3 — Stage the transcript

```
git add agents/<agent>/transcripts/<YYYY-MM-DD>-<short-uuid>.md
```

Verify the file is staged with `git status --short`.

## Step 4 — (reserved for condenser, no-op in Phase 1)

Log `end-session: condenser step skipped — Phase 2 will wire Syndra's component A here` and continue.

## Step 5 — Journal append

Prompt the invoking agent (you, running this skill) to append their first-person reflection for this session to `agents/<agent>/journal/cli-<YYYY-MM-DD>.md`. Rules:

- Append only. Do NOT overwrite existing content.
- First-person voice. Not a transcript copy.
- 10–30 lines typical. No hard cap.

Use the Write tool if the file does not exist, Edit (append) if it does. After writing, stage the file:

```
git add agents/<agent>/journal/cli-<YYYY-MM-DD>.md
```

## Step 6 — Remember handoff

**If agent == evelynn:** Skip the `remember:remember` plugin entirely (it has a single-file race surface unsafe under concurrent close — see D6 in `plans/approved/2026-04-18-evelynn-memory-sharding.md`). Instead, write a new shard at `agents/evelynn/memory/last-sessions/<short-uuid>.md` where `<short-uuid>` is the UUID from Step 2's transcript path. Content: a structured 5–10 line handoff — date, session number, what happened, open threads, dangling commits or PRs, blockers. Stage:

```
git add agents/evelynn/memory/last-sessions/<short-uuid>.md
```

Note "remember:remember bypassed for evelynn — shard written to last-sessions/<short-uuid>.md" in the final report.

**If agent != evelynn:** Invoke the `remember:remember` skill via the Skill tool. This is the primary handoff mechanism — it writes `.remember/remember.md` with a structured snapshot of what is done, what is next, and any non-obvious context. The Remember plugin's `SessionStart` hook loads this automatically at the start of the next session.

```
Skill: remember:remember
```

Stage the output file:

```
git add .remember/remember.md
```

If the `remember` plugin is not installed or the skill is unavailable, fall back to writing `agents/<agent>/memory/last-session.md` manually with a 5–10 line terse handoff (date, what happened, open threads, dangling commits or PRs, blockers). Stage with `git add -f agents/<agent>/memory/last-session.md`. Note "remember step skipped — plugin not available, used last-session.md fallback" in the final report.

## Step 6b — Update open-threads.md + regenerate INDEX.md (coordinators only)

**Ordering invariant:** Step 6 (write shard) MUST complete before Step 6b because the shard is the source for both open-threads.md and INDEX.md updates. Step 6b MUST complete before Step 9 (commit + push) so all three artifacts land atomically in one commit.

**If agent is a coordinator (evelynn OR sona):** Run the following after Step 6 completes.

1. Parse the shard's `## Open threads into next session` section (or `## Open threads` section). For each thread listed:
   - If resolved/closed: remove or mark closed the matching `## <thread>` section in `agents/<agent>/memory/open-threads.md`.
   - If new or still-open: add or update its `## <thread>` section with the shard UUID as a pointer and a status one-liner.
   - You are the coordinator — you confirm the diff before writing. Hand-curation is the value here.
   - If `open-threads.md` does not exist yet, create it from scratch.

2. Stage:
   ```
   git add agents/<agent>/memory/open-threads.md
   ```

3. Regenerate `last-sessions/INDEX.md`:
   ```
   bash scripts/memory-consolidate.sh <agent> --index-only
   ```

4. Stage:
   ```
   git add agents/<agent>/memory/last-sessions/INDEX.md
   ```

If Step 6b fails partway (e.g., `--index-only` errors), the shard written in Step 6 is already staged and recoverable. Do NOT abort the session close — log the failure and proceed to Step 9 with only the shard staged. Recovery path: run `bash scripts/memory-consolidate.sh <agent> --index-only`, stage `INDEX.md`, and amend the next commit manually.

**If agent is NOT a coordinator (non-coordinator agents — Sonnet subagents, Lissandra standalone, etc.):** Step 6b is a no-op. Skip entirely and proceed to Step 7.

## Step 7 — Memory refresh

**If agent == evelynn:** Do NOT touch `agents/evelynn/memory/evelynn.md`. Instead, write a new shard at `agents/evelynn/memory/sessions/<short-uuid>.md` (same UUID from Step 2) containing:
- A `## Session YYYY-MM-DD (SN, <mode>)` heading.
- One-line summary of the session.
- Any delta notes to Key Context or Working Patterns that should be folded in at next consolidation.

Stage the shard:

```
git add agents/evelynn/memory/sessions/<short-uuid>.md
```

Note "evelynn memory shard written to sessions/<short-uuid>.md — consolidation will fold into evelynn.md at next boot" in the final report.

**If agent != evelynn:** Review `agents/<agent>/memory/<agent>.md`. If anything material changed this session (new working patterns, new known issues, sessions list), update it:

- Append a new session row to the `## Sessions` list with the format `- YYYY-MM-DD (SN, <mode>): <one-line summary>`.
- Prune stale entries if the file exceeds 50 lines. Remove the oldest session rows first.
- Update `## Key context` or `## Working patterns` only if the change is durable.

If nothing material changed, skip the update but still state "no memory changes this session" in the final report. Stage if modified:

```
git add agents/<agent>/memory/<agent>.md
```

## Step 8 — Learnings

If this session produced a generalizable lesson (something a future instance of this agent or a sibling agent would benefit from), write it to `agents/<agent>/learnings/<YYYY-MM-DD>-<topic>.md` and add a one-line reference to `agents/<agent>/learnings/index.md`.

If no learning, skip and state "no learnings this session" in the final report.

Stage any new learning files:

```
git add agents/<agent>/learnings/
```

## Step 9 — Commit + push

Build the commit message. Format:

```
chore: <agent> session closing — transcript, handoff, memory, learnings for YYYY-MM-DD <platform> session
```

Use `cli` as the platform for Claude Code sessions. Use HEREDOC form:

```
git commit -m "$(cat <<'EOF'
chore: <agent> session closing — transcript, handoff, memory, learnings for YYYY-MM-DD <platform> session

Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.6 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
EOF
)"
```

Then push:

```
git push
```

**If the pre-push hook rejects the commit** (wrong prefix, gitleaks hit, anything): STOP. Do not retry. Do not rewrite the commit. Report the error verbatim in the final report and exit with `end-session: commit rejected — manual intervention required`.

**If the push fails because main moved forward**: pull with merge (never rebase per CLAUDE.md git rules), then re-push. One retry only. If the second push fails, stop and report.

## Step 10 — Final report

Print a single-paragraph summary to the agent's output:

- Cleaned transcript path
- Commit hash
- Push status
- Journal / remember handoff / memory / learnings status (which were updated, which were skipped)
- Any warnings from the chain-walk or non-fatal errors along the way

Then exit. Do not close the session yourself — Duong or Evelynn explicitly ends the session after reviewing the report.

# /end-session — top-level session close

You are closing a top-level Claude Code session. This skill wraps the full close-session protocol into a deterministic checklist. Follow every step in order. Do not skip steps. Do not reorder.

## Argument

`evelynn` is the agent name whose session is being closed. If empty, refuse immediately with `end-session: agent name required — pass the agent name as an argument (e.g. /end-session evelynn)` and exit. If `evelynn` is set to something other than a valid agent name (no matching `agents/<name>/` directory), refuse with `end-session: unknown agent <name>` and exit.

## Step 0 — Context probe

Run these Bash commands in a single call and keep the output in mind:

```
pwd
git status --short
git log -1 --oneline
date -u +%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%SZ
```

If the working tree has uncommitted changes unrelated to the session close (files outside `agents/<agent>/`, `scripts/`, `CLAUDE.md`, `.gitignore`), stop and report: `end-session: working tree dirty with unrelated files — commit or stash before closing`. Do not proceed.

## Step 1 — Discover source jsonl

Run the cleaner in dry-run mode (just discovery, no write) using the Bash tool:

```
python scripts/clean-jsonl.py --agent <agent> --session auto --out /tmp/end-session-probe.md
```

Note: for Phase 1, the cleaner does not have a separate dry-run flag. The `/tmp/` output path is a throwaway probe. After the probe, delete `/tmp/end-session-probe.md`.

Capture the stderr for any `CLEANER: chain ambiguous` warnings and relay them to the agent for confirmation before proceeding.

## Step 2 — Clean transcript

Run the cleaner for real:

```
python scripts/clean-jsonl.py --agent <agent> --session auto
```

The cleaner writes to the default path `agents/<agent>/transcripts/<YYYY-MM-DD>-<short-uuid>.md`.

- On exit code 0: record the output path from the cleaner's stdout.
- On exit code 1: report the error and stop. Do not proceed to any further step.
- On exit code 2: report the internal error and stop.
- On exit code 3: report the secret match verbatim, STOP IMMEDIATELY, do not stage any files, do not run the commit step. Escalate to Duong via the final report.

## Step 3 — Stage the transcript

```
git add agents/<agent>/transcripts/<YYYY-MM-DD>-<short-uuid>.md
```

Verify the file is staged with `git status --short`.

## Step 4 — (reserved for condenser, no-op in Phase 1)

Log `end-session: condenser step skipped — Phase 2 will wire Syndra's component A here` and continue.

## Step 5 — Journal append

Prompt the invoking agent (you, running this skill) to append their first-person reflection for this session to `agents/<agent>/journal/cli-<YYYY-MM-DD>.md`. Rules:

- Append only. Do NOT overwrite existing content.
- First-person voice. Not a transcript copy.
- 10–30 lines typical. No hard cap.

Use the Write tool if the file does not exist, Edit (append) if it does. After writing, stage the file:

```
git add agents/<agent>/journal/cli-<YYYY-MM-DD>.md
```

## Step 6 — Remember handoff

**If agent == evelynn:** Skip the `remember:remember` plugin entirely (it has a single-file race surface unsafe under concurrent close — see D6 in `plans/approved/2026-04-18-evelynn-memory-sharding.md`). Instead, write a new shard at `agents/evelynn/memory/last-sessions/<short-uuid>.md` where `<short-uuid>` is the UUID from Step 2's transcript path. Content: a structured 5–10 line handoff — date, session number, what happened, open threads, dangling commits or PRs, blockers. Stage:

```
git add agents/evelynn/memory/last-sessions/<short-uuid>.md
```

Note "remember:remember bypassed for evelynn — shard written to last-sessions/<short-uuid>.md" in the final report.

**If agent != evelynn:** Invoke the `remember:remember` skill via the Skill tool. This is the primary handoff mechanism — it writes `.remember/remember.md` with a structured snapshot of what is done, what is next, and any non-obvious context. The Remember plugin's `SessionStart` hook loads this automatically at the start of the next session.

```
Skill: remember:remember
```

Stage the output file:

```
git add .remember/remember.md
```

If the `remember` plugin is not installed or the skill is unavailable, fall back to writing `agents/<agent>/memory/last-session.md` manually with a 5–10 line terse handoff (date, what happened, open threads, dangling commits or PRs, blockers). Stage with `git add -f agents/<agent>/memory/last-session.md`. Note "remember step skipped — plugin not available, used last-session.md fallback" in the final report.

## Step 6b — Update open-threads.md + regenerate INDEX.md (coordinators only)

**Ordering invariant:** Step 6 (write shard) MUST complete before Step 6b because the shard is the source for both open-threads.md and INDEX.md updates. Step 6b MUST complete before Step 9 (commit + push) so all three artifacts land atomically in one commit.

**If agent is a coordinator (evelynn OR sona):** Run the following after Step 6 completes.

1. Parse the shard's `## Open threads into next session` section (or `## Open threads` section). For each thread listed:
   - If resolved/closed: remove or mark closed the matching `## <thread>` section in `agents/<agent>/memory/open-threads.md`.
   - If new or still-open: add or update its `## <thread>` section with the shard UUID as a pointer and a status one-liner.
   - You are the coordinator — you confirm the diff before writing. Hand-curation is the value here.
   - If `open-threads.md` does not exist yet, create it from scratch.

2. Stage:
   ```
   git add agents/<agent>/memory/open-threads.md
   ```

3. Regenerate `last-sessions/INDEX.md`:
   ```
   bash scripts/memory-consolidate.sh <agent> --index-only
   ```

4. Stage:
   ```
   git add agents/<agent>/memory/last-sessions/INDEX.md
   ```

If Step 6b fails partway (e.g., `--index-only` errors), the shard written in Step 6 is already staged and recoverable. Do NOT abort the session close — log the failure and proceed to Step 9 with only the shard staged. Recovery path: run `bash scripts/memory-consolidate.sh <agent> --index-only`, stage `INDEX.md`, and amend the next commit manually.

**If agent is NOT a coordinator (non-coordinator agents — Sonnet subagents, Lissandra standalone, etc.):** Step 6b is a no-op. Skip entirely and proceed to Step 7.

## Step 7 — Memory refresh

**If agent == evelynn:** Do NOT touch `agents/evelynn/memory/evelynn.md`. Instead, write a new shard at `agents/evelynn/memory/sessions/<short-uuid>.md` (same UUID from Step 2) containing:
- A `## Session YYYY-MM-DD (SN, <mode>)` heading.
- One-line summary of the session.
- Any delta notes to Key Context or Working Patterns that should be folded in at next consolidation.

Stage the shard:

```
git add agents/evelynn/memory/sessions/<short-uuid>.md
```

Note "evelynn memory shard written to sessions/<short-uuid>.md — consolidation will fold into evelynn.md at next boot" in the final report.

**If agent != evelynn:** Review `agents/<agent>/memory/<agent>.md`. If anything material changed this session (new working patterns, new known issues, sessions list), update it:

- Append a new session row to the `## Sessions` list with the format `- YYYY-MM-DD (SN, <mode>): <one-line summary>`.
- Prune stale entries if the file exceeds 50 lines. Remove the oldest session rows first.
- Update `## Key context` or `## Working patterns` only if the change is durable.

If nothing material changed, skip the update but still state "no memory changes this session" in the final report. Stage if modified:

```
git add agents/<agent>/memory/<agent>.md
```

## Step 8 — Learnings

If this session produced a generalizable lesson (something a future instance of this agent or a sibling agent would benefit from), write it to `agents/<agent>/learnings/<YYYY-MM-DD>-<topic>.md` and add a one-line reference to `agents/<agent>/learnings/index.md`.

If no learning, skip and state "no learnings this session" in the final report.

Stage any new learning files:

```
git add agents/<agent>/learnings/
```

## Step 9 — Commit + push

Build the commit message. Format:

```
chore: <agent> session closing — transcript, handoff, memory, learnings for YYYY-MM-DD <platform> session
```

Use `cli` as the platform for Claude Code sessions. Use HEREDOC form:

```
git commit -m "$(cat <<'EOF'
chore: <agent> session closing — transcript, handoff, memory, learnings for YYYY-MM-DD <platform> session

Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.6 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
EOF
)"
```

Then push:

```
git push
```

**If the pre-push hook rejects the commit** (wrong prefix, gitleaks hit, anything): STOP. Do not retry. Do not rewrite the commit. Report the error verbatim in the final report and exit with `end-session: commit rejected — manual intervention required`.

**If the push fails because main moved forward**: pull with merge (never rebase per CLAUDE.md git rules), then re-push. One retry only. If the second push fails, stop and report.

## Step 10 — Final report

Print a single-paragraph summary to the agent's output:

- Cleaned transcript path
- Commit hash
- Push status
- Journal / remember handoff / memory / learnings status (which were updated, which were skipped)
- Any warnings from the chain-walk or non-fatal errors along the way

Then exit. Do not close the session yourself — Duong or Evelynn explicitly ends the session after reviewing the report.
